Al-Talwih and Its Author: Key Sources of Hanafi Usul
Biographical and bibliographical description of al-Talwih and al-Taftazani

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual lineage of al-Talwih and explain the scholarly significance of al-Taftazani in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Talwih is a super-commentary that unlocks the depths of al-Tanqih, and its author al-Taftazani was a towering polymath of the 8th century.

This lesson introduces the work al-Talwih and its author, the renowned scholar Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. Understanding this text's place in the Hanafi tradition helps you navigate the usul literature and appreciate the scholarly chain of transmission and commentary.

Guided Path
1
Locate the work in the commentary chain
Identify that al-Tanqih is the base text, al-Tawdih is its commentary, and al-Talwih is a commentary on al-Tawdih. This is a standard super-commentary structure in Hanafi usul.
The base text al-Tanqih is by the Hanafi scholar al-Mahbubi (صاحب الوقاية).
2
Note the author's full name and key dates
Recognize al-Taftazani's full name: Mas'ud bin Umar bin Abdullah Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. He completed al-Talwih in 758 AH (or 756 AH per another account) in Turkestan.
His date of death is disputed; Ibn Hajar suggests 792 AH.
3
Assess the author's scholarly range
From the biography, note his expertise in grammar, morphology, rhetoric, logic, and other fields. He began writing at age 16 and was renowned across the Islamic world.
He had a lisp, which may have affected his speech but not his writings.
4
Understand the text's purpose
Al-Talwih (meaning 'illumination') was written to delve into the benefits of al-Tanqih and to clarify its realities. It is a verbal commentary that expands on al-Tawdih.
The preface praises Allah for establishing the foundations of Sharia.
5
Relate to Hanafi usul
This work is a standard reference in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Knowing its place in the commentary chain helps you assess authority and navigate the literature.
Al-Talwih is often cited alongside al-Tawdih in later Hanafi works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٩ التلويح: هو شرح التوضيح للعلامة مسعود بن عمر بن عبد الله سعد الدين التفتازاني. وهو شرح بالقول أوله الحمد لله الذى أحكم بكتابه أصول الشريعة الغراء... إلخ. ذكر أن التنقيح مع شرحه التوضيح كتاب شامل الخلاصة كل مبسوط فأراد الخوض في لجج فوائده وسماه بـ التلويح في كشف حقائق التنقيح، وفرغ عنه في سلخ ذى القعدة سنة ثمان وخمسين وسبعمائة (٧٥٨) في بلدة من تركستان، كذا في الكشف. وفى الفوائد: أنه فرغ من التلويح فى ذى القعدة سنة ٧٥٦ بكلستان وتركستان فافهم. والتوضيح هو شرح التنقيح وهما لصاحب الوقاية. وقد ذكرنا ترجمته في فهرس الأعلام فراجعه إن شئت. والتفتازاني: وهو مسعود بن عمر بن عبد الله، سعد الدين، التفتازاني، الإمام العلامة، عالم بالنحو والتصريف، والمعاني والبيان والمنطق وغيرها. أخذ عن ا. القطب والعضد، وتقدم في الفنون، واشتهر ذكره، وطار صيته، وانتفع الناس بتصانيفه وكان منفرداً في العلوم في القرن الثامن. قال ابن حجر: انتهت إليه معرفة علوم البلاغة والمعقول بالمشرق بل بسائر الأمصار، لم يكن له نظير في معرفة هذه العلوم. وكانت في لسانه لكنة، أخذ في تصنيف الكتب وهو ابن ست عشرة سنة، وأول تصانيفه الإرشاد في النحو واتصل إلى السلطان تيمور لنك، وكان عنده بمكانة وفي مجلسه جرت المناظرة بينه وبين السيد الشريف أحمد الجرجاني في "أن الانتقام سبب الغضب أم الغضب سبب الانتقام". فكان العلامة قائلا بالأول والثاني بالثاني. وكان الشيخ أبو منصور الكارزونى حكماً بينهما، مرجح قول السيد، فاغتم العلامة لأجله عما شديداً حتى قيل: إنه كان سبب موته. وذكر ابن حجر فى سنة وفاته قولين: الأول: سنة ٧٩٢هـ
19. Al-Talwih: It is a commentary on al-Tawdih by the scholar Mas'ud bin Umar bin Abdullah Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani. It is a verbal commentary; its beginning: 'Praise be to Allah who established with His book the foundations of the noble Sharia... etc.' He mentioned that al-Tanqih with its commentary al-Tawdih is a book that includes the essence of every extensive work, so he wanted to delve into the depths of its benefits and named it al-Talwih fi Kashf Haqa'iq al-Tanqih. He completed it at the end of Dhu al-Qa'dah in the year 758 AH in a town in Turkestan, according to al-Kashf. And in al-Fawa'id: that he completed al-Talwih in Dhu al-Qa'dah 756 in Gulistan and Turkestan, so understand. Al-Tawdih is a commentary on al-Tanqih, both by the author of al-Wiqayah. We have mentioned his biography in the index of notables, so refer to it if you wish. Al-Taftazani: He is Mas'ud bin Umar bin Abdullah, Sa'd al-Din, al-Taftazani, the imam, the scholar, versed in grammar, morphology, rhetoric, logic, and other fields. He studied under [?] al-Qutb and al-‘Adud, and excelled in the arts; his fame spread, and people benefited from his works. He was unique in the sciences in the eighth century. Ibn Hajar said: The knowledge of rhetorical and rational sciences culminated in him in the East and in all lands; he had no peer in knowing these sciences. He had a lisp in his tongue. He began authoring books at the age of sixteen; his first work was al-Irshad on grammar. He connected with Sultan Timur Lang, and held a position with him. In his court, a debate occurred between him and Sayyid Sharif Ahmad al-Jurjani regarding 'Is revenge the cause of anger or anger the cause of revenge?' The scholar (al-Taftazani) said the first, and the second (al-Jurjani) said the second. Shaykh Abu Mansur al-Karizuni was the judge between them, giving preference to the sayyid's statement. The scholar became extremely distressed by that, and it is said that was the cause of his death. Ibn Hajar mentioned two opinions regarding his death year: the first is 792 AH.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage introduces the book al-Talwih, which is a commentary by al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih (itself a commentary on al-Tanqih by the author of al-Wiqayah). It also provides a detailed biography of al-Taftazani, a polymath expert in many fields, and recounts a famous debate with al-Jurjani that allegedly caused his death. The entry serves as a reference source for this Hanafi usul work.

Key Terms
التلويح (al-Talwih): A commentary on al-Tawdih by al-Taftazani, in the field of usul al-fiqh.
التنقيح (al-Tanqih): The base text on Hanafi usul al-fiqh by al-Mahbubi (sahib al-Wiqayah).
التوضيح (al-Tawdih): A commentary on al-Tanqih by the same author (al-Mahbubi).
التفتازاني (al-Taftazani): The scholar Mas'ud bin Umar bin Abdullah Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, author of al-Talwih and many other works.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Al-Talwih is a super-commentary by al-Taftazani on al-Tawdih, itself a commentary on al-Tanqih, and it is a key source in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Parsing a Hanafi Fiqh Bibliography: The List of Works in Sharh al-'Uqud
Bibliography of Hanafi works cited in the commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a Hanafi fiqh bibliography entry, identify the work, author, death date, and its print/manuscript status, and explain why such lists are essential for establishing textual authority in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Core Idea
A Hanafi fiqh bibliography is a map of the madhhab's authoritative sources — mastering it is the first step to proper tarjih and fatwa.

This passage lists works cited in the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. At first glance, it is a simple list of book titles and authors. But for a mufti, this list is a critical tool: it identifies which sources the commentator considered authoritative, notes which works remained in manuscript, and sometimes clarifies authorship disputes. In this lesson, you will learn how to read such a bibliography, extract key details, and understand its role in the Hanafi textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry number
Each entry is numbered (30–36). This helps reference and shows the list is part of a larger catalog.
2
Extract the work title
The title is given first, often with a descriptive phrase. For example, 'Hashiyah al-Ramli 'ala al-Bahr'. Note that some works are known by multiple names.
The title may include 'hashiyah', 'hawi', 'hukm', etc.
3
Identify the author and his full name
The author's name, including lineage and nisbah, is provided. Death dates are given in Hijri. For some entries, the author's biography is summarized.
Death dates are crucial for establishing the work's place in the historical chain of authority.
4
Note the work's status
The passage explicitly states whether the work is printed (matbu') or manuscript (makhṭūṭ). Sometimes it says 'not printed until now'. This affects the work's accessibility and authority.
Manuscripts may be rare or difficult to verify.
5
Check for additional notes on authorship
For some entries, like al-Hawi al-Qudsi, there is a discussion about the correct author. This is important because a misattribution can undermine a fatwa's authority.
The author uses 'qila' (it is said) and other phrases to indicate uncertainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح

۳۰ حاشية الرملى على البحر : وهى مظهر الحقائق على البحر الرائق للعلامة خير الدين الرملي المتقدم ذكره في الفتاوى الخيرية في الكتب. وحاشيته هذه لم تطبع إلى الآن. ونقل هذه العبارة (أى) المذكورة في شرح العقود) العلامة الشامي في حاشيته على البحر المسماة بـ منحة الخالق .
-۳۱- حاشية الطحطاوي على الدر المختار: وهي كما قال الشامي في شرح العقود الخاتمة الفقهاء والعباد الناسكين مفتى مصر القاهرة، سيدى المرحوم، السيد أحمد بن محمد الطحطاوي (الطهطاوى)، المتوفى سنة ١٢٣١هـ. فقيه حنفی مشهور . وهو من فضلاء القرن الثالث عشر كما يظهر من مطالعة كتاب الإجارات من رد المحتار .
وقد تتملذ عليه عبد المولى بن عبد الله الدمياطى صاحب تعاليق الأنوار على الدر المختار . قال في مفيد المفتى : إنه مات سنة ١٢٤٣هـ . وقيل : "سنة ١٢٣٣هـ . كما في الحدائق. وفي غيث الغمام ( ص ٣٦) : "أنه مات سنة ١٢٥٠هـ " ، وله كتابان مطبوعان: ۱- حاشية الطحطاوي على الدر المختار في أربعة مجلدات ضخمة . -۲ حاشية الطحطاوي على المراقى ورسالة كشف الرين عن بيان المسح على الجوربين " مخطوطة .
-
-۳۲ حاشية الهداية للخبازى : هى للشيخ جلال الدين أبي محمد عمر ابن محمد بن عمر الخبازي، الحجندي الدمشقي، المولود سنة ٦٢٩ ، المتوفى سنة إحدى وتسعين وستمائة ، حاشية مشهورة ،مخطوطة، أخذها محمد بن أحمد القونوي وكملها إلى آخر الهداية، وسماها تكملة الفوائد. كذا فى الفوائد وفيه أيضًا. قال الجامع : أرخ صاحب الكشف وفاته سنة إحدى وسبعين وستمائة . وله المغنى في أصول الفقه . مخطوط وانظر في فهرس الأعلام : جلال الدين الخبازى .
۳۳- الحاوى القدسى : قال الحموي في حواشي الأشباه : قيل : الحاوي لأصحابنا اثنان الحاوى القدسي : وأظنه لرجل متأخر يسمى قاضي القدس ولا أعرف تفصیل ترجمته وكتابه غیر مطبوع والحاوى الحصيرى : وهو للشيخ محمد

۲۱۳
الكتب الواردة في الشرح ابن إبراهيم ابن أنوش الحصيرى (المنوفى ٥٠٠هـ) . وهي أيضا مخطوطة. كان من تلامذة شمس الأئمة، وترجمته بـ ذیل تاریخ بغداد للسمعانی ولم يذكره عبد القادر في طبقاته، ولا الشيخ قاسم بن قطلوبغا. انتهى . أقول : بقى حاوى ثالث : وهو "حاوى الزاهدى ومؤلفه صاحب القنية وهو عزيز الوحود، ومخطوطة حتى الآن. ورأيت عند بعض شيوخنا منه نسخة . انتهى .
قلت : ذكر ابن الشحنة فى هوامش الجواهر : أن الحاوى القدسي للقاضي جمال الذين أحمد بن محمد بن نوح القابسي الغزنوي، الحنفي، المتوفي في حدود سنة ستمائة . وإنما قيل له : القدسى؛ لأنه صنفه في القدس. نقلته من خط تلميذه حسن ابن على النحوى. انتهى. كذا نقله صاحب الكشف، ثم قال : ورأيت على ظهر نسخة منه : أن مصنفه الإمام محمد الغزنوى أوله الحمد لله الذي هدانا لدين الإسلام ... إلخ. انتهى . ثم ذكر صاحب الكشف الحاوى للزاهدى" وهو مختار ابن محمود الغزميني أوله الحمد لله الذى أوضح معالم العلوم . . . إلخ ثم ذكر : الحاوى في الفروع لنجم الدين أبى شجاع، وأبى الفضائل بكير التركي، المتوفى سنة ٦٥٢هـ . وذكر ابن أمير حاج الحلبي في شرح منية المصلى : أن مؤلف الحاوى القدسي فرغاني . أفاده الشيخ العلامة عبد الحي اللكوى في الفوائد البهية .
•
1
الحقائق : هو حقائق المنظومة شرح منظومة النسعى لأبي المحامد محمود ابن محمد بن داود الإفسنجى اللؤلؤى البخاري. وهو فقيه، محدث، حافظ، ،مفسر أصولى منكلم أديب . له التوسع فى الكلام والجدل ولد ببخارى سنة سبع وعشرين وستمائة، واستشهد في وقعة بحاري سنة إحدى وسبعين وستمائة . وشرحه هذا بديع الأسلوب، بداولته العلماء . مكت في جمعه أكثر من سبع سنين، وأتمه يوم عيد الأضحى سنة ست وسنين وستمائة ببخارى ومخطوطته موجودة بالمدينة المنورة.
-
-۳٥ حواشي الكشف : يحتمل أن المراد به كشف الأسرار شرح المنار صاحب لكبر، أن كشف الأسرار سرح أصول البزدوى لعبد العزيز بن أحمد البخاري المتوفى سنة تلاى وسعمائة . ٣٦- الحيل : هي كتاب الجبل للحصاف وهو احمد بن عـمـر الـنـاني
The books mentioned in the commentary:
30. Hashiyah al-Ramli 'ala al-Bahr: It is Mazhar al-Haqa'iq 'ala al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by the scholar Khayr al-Din al-Ramli, previously mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah among the books. This hashiah of his has not been printed until now. The phrase (i.e., mentioned in Sharh al-'Uqud) was transmitted by the scholar al-Shami in his hashiah on al-Bahr named Minhat al-Khaliq.
31. Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar: It is, as al-Shami said in Sharh al-'Uqud, the seal of jurists and devout worshippers, the mufti of Cairo, my late master, Sayyid Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Tahtawi (al-Tahatawi), died 1231 AH. A famous Hanafi jurist. He was one of the distinguished scholars of the 13th century, as seen from reading the book of rentals (al-Ijarat) from Radd al-Muhtar. 'Abd al-Mawla ibn 'Abd Allah al-Dimyati, author of Ta'aliq al-Anwar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar, was his student. In Mufid al-Mufti, he said he died in 1243 AH. And it is said: 1233 AH, as in al-Hada'iq. In Ghayth al-Ghamam (p. 36): that he died in 1250 AH. He has two printed books: 1. Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar in four large volumes. 2. Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Maraqi and a manuscript treatise Kashf al-Rayn 'an Bayan al-Mash 'ala al-Jawrabayn.
32. Hashiyah al-Hidayah li al-Khabbazi: It is by Shaykh Jalal al-Din Abi Muhammad 'Umar ibn Muhammad ibn 'Umar al-Khabbazi, al-Hujandi al-Dimashqi, born 629, died 691 AH. A famous manuscript hashiah. Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Qunawi took it and completed it to the end of al-Hidayah, naming it Takmilat al-Fawa'id. Thus in al-Fawa'id and also. Al-Jami' said: The author of Kashf recorded his death as 671 AH. He also has al-Mughni fi Usul al-Fiqh, manuscript. See in Fihris al-A'lam: Jalal al-Din al-Khabbazi.
33. Al-Hawi al-Qudsi: Al-Hamawi said in Hawashi al-Ashbah: It is said al-Hawi for our companions is two: al-Hawi al-Qudsi: I think it is for a later man called Qadi al-Quds, and I do not know the details of his biography, and his book is unprinted; and al-Hawi al-Hasiri: It is by Shaykh Muhammad ibn Ibrahim ibn Anush al-Hasiri (al-Manufi 500 AH). It is also a manuscript. He was a student of Shams al-A'imma, and his biography is in Dhayl Tarikh Baghdad by al-Sam'ani, and 'Abd al-Qadir did not mention him in his Tabaqat, nor did Shaykh Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. End. I say: There remains a third Hawi: namely Hawi al-Zahidi, and its author is the author of al-Qunyah, and it is rare, a manuscript until now. I saw a copy of it with some of our shaykhs. End.
I say: Ibn al-Shihnah mentioned in the margins of al-Jawahir: that al-Hawi al-Qudsi is by Qadi Jamal al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Nuh al-Qabisi al-Ghaznawi, al-Hanafi, who died around 600 AH. It was called al-Qudsi because he compiled it in Jerusalem. I copied it from the handwriting of his student Hasan ibn 'Ali al-Nahwi. End. Thus transmitted by the author of Kashf, then he said: I saw on the cover of a copy of it: that its author is Imam Muhammad al-Ghaznawi; its beginning: 'Praise be to Allah who guided us to the religion of Islam...' etc. End. Then the author of Kashf mentioned al-Hawi li al-Zahidi, which is Mukhtar ibn Mahmud al-Ghazmini, its beginning: 'Praise be to Allah who clarified the marks of the sciences...' etc. Then he mentioned al-Hawi fi al-Furu' by Najm al-Din Abi Shuja' and Abi al-Fada'il Bakir al-Turki, died 652 AH. Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi was Farghani. This was informed by the scholar 'Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah.
34. Al-Haqa'iq: It is Haqa'iq al-Manzumah, a commentary on Manzumah al-Nasa'i by Abi al-Mahamid Mahmud ibn Muhammad ibn Dawud al-Isfanji al-Lu'lu'i al-Bukhari. He was a jurist, muhaddith, hafiz, mufassir, usuli, mutakallim, and litterateur. He was expansive in discourse and debate. He was born in Bukhara in 627 AH and martyred in the battle of Bukhara in 671 AH. This commentary of his is of excellent style, circulated among scholars. He spent more than seven years compiling it and completed it on the day of 'Eid al-Adha in 666 AH in Bukhara, and its manuscript is in Medina.
35. Hawashi al-Kashf: It is likely that it means Kashf al-Asrar, a commentary on al-Manar by the author of al-Kubra, that Kashf al-Asrar is a commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi by 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari who died around 700 AH.
36. Al-Hiyal: It is the book al-Hiyal by al-Hassaf, who is Ahmad ibn 'Umar al-Nasafi.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage forms part of the front matter of the commentary on 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. It lists the works cited in the commentary, providing brief biographical details about each author and the status of their works. The author methodically enumerates these references to establish the authority of the sources used. The list covers manuscripts such as Hashiyah al-Ramli, Hashiyah al-Tahtawi, Hashiyah al-Khabbazi, al-Hawi al-Qudsi, al-Haqa'iq, Hawashi al-Kashf, and al-Hiyal. For each, he notes whether the work is printed or manuscript, the author's death date, and sometimes clarifies disputes about authorship, as seen in the discussion about al-Hawi al-Qudsi. This section is essential for the student of Hanafi fiqh to understand the textual hierarchy and the chain of authorities in the later tradition.

Key Terms
حاشية (hashiyah): A supercommentary or gloss on a primary text; this passage mentions several such works on al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Hidayah.
الحاوي (al-Hawi): A comprehensive compendium of Hanafi fiqh; multiple works with this title are listed, including al-Hawi al-Qudsi and al-Hawi al-Hasiri.
مخطوطة (makhṭūṭah): Manuscript; the passage notes which works remain unprinted and exist only in manuscript form.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following works is explicitly mentioned as being unprinted (not yet printed) at the time of writing?
A) Hashiyah al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar
B) Hashiyah al-Ramli 'ala al-Bahr
C) Al-Hawi al-Hasiri
D) Al-Haqa'iq

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi fiqh bibliography is not just a list — it is a critical tool for verifying the authority of sources used in fatwa.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
6 min
The Hawī Compendia: A Mufti's Source Guide
Biographical listing of multiple Hanafi 'Hawi' compendia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the various 'Hawi' compendia in the Hanafi tradition, identifying their authors, approximate dates, and significance for fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Not all 'Hawi' works are the same—distinguishing them is key to tracing fatwa sources and authorship.

This lesson guides you through a passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti that lists several important 'Hawi' compendia. These works are comprehensive fiqh collections that a mufti may encounter when researching authoritative positions. Understanding which 'Hawi' is being cited helps assess its reliability and scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify each named work
Read the passage and list every distinct 'Hawi' title mentioned. Note that some appear under slightly different names (e.g., 'Hawi al-Zahidi' appears twice with different authors).
Keep track of full titles as they appear.
2
Associate each work with its author
For each Hawi, find the author's name, along with any epithets or additional details (e.g., 'author of al-Qunyah', 'Judge Jamal al-Din').
Authors are key: later fatwa collections often refer to a Hawi by its author's name.
3
Note the date or period of each work
The passage provides death dates for some authors (e.g., d. 500 AH, d. 652 AH). For others, an approximate period is given. Record these to understand the chronological order.
Dates help determine which works were available to later scholars.
4
Identify distinguishing features
Observe unique attributes: 'al-Qudsi' is named because it was written in Jerusalem; 'Hawi al-Zahidi' is rare; some works are manuscripts. These features affect how a mufti evaluates the source.
Such details are often noted in biographical entries.
5
Understand the significance for fatwa
Reflect on why a mufti would need to know these distinctions: citing the correct Hawi ensures accurate attribution and reliability. The passage itself is an example of the meticulous source criticism required in usul al-ifta.
Knowing the author and status (manuscript, rare, etc.) informs the mufti's reliance on a given work.

الكتب الواردة في الشرح ابن إبراهيم ابن أنوش الحصيرى (المتوفى ٥٠٠هـ). وهي أيضا مخطوطة. كان من تلامذة شمس الأئمة، وترجمته بـ ذيل تاريخ بغداد للسمعاني ولم يذكره عبد القادر في طبقاته، ولا الشيخ قاسم بن قطلوبغا. انتهى. أقول: بقي حاوي ثالث: وهو "حاوي الزاهدى" ومؤلفه صاحب القنية وهو عزيز الوجود، ومخطوطة حتى الآن. ورأيت عند بعض شيوخنا منه نسخة. انتهى. قلت: ذكر ابن الشحنة في هوامش الجواهر: أن الحاوي القدسي للقاضي جمال الدين أحمد بن محمد بن نوح القابسي الغزنوي، الحنفي، المتوفي في حدود سنة ستمائة. وإنما قيل له: القدسي؛ لأنه صنفه في القدس. نقلته من خط تلميذه حسن بن علي النحوي. انتهى. كذا نقله صاحب الكشف، ثم قال: ورأيت على ظهر نسخة منه: أن مصنفه الإمام محمد الغزنوي أوله الحمد لله الذي هدانا لدين الإسلام... إلخ. انتهى. ثم ذكر صاحب الكشف الحاوي للزاهدى" وهو مختار ابن محمود الغزميني أوله الحمد لله الذي أوضح معالم العلوم... إلخ. ثم ذكر: الحاوي في الفروع لنجم الدين أبي شجاع، وأبي الفضائل بكير التركي، المتوفى سنة ٦٥٢هـ. وذكر ابن أمير حاج الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي: أن مؤلف الحاوي القدسي فرغاني. أفاده الشيخ العلامة عبد الحي اللكوي في الفوائد البهية.
The books mentioned in the commentary: Ibn Ibrahim Ibn Anush al-Hasiri (d. 500 AH). It is also a manuscript. He was a student of Shams al-A'imma, and his biography is in the supplement to Tarikh Baghdad by al-Sam'ani; Abdul Qadir did not mention him in his Tabaqat, nor did Shaykh Qasim bin Qutlubugha. End. I say: A third Hawi remains: it is 'Hawi al-Zahidi' and its author is the author of al-Qunyah, and it is rare in existence, and a manuscript until now. I saw a copy of it with some of our teachers. End. I said: Ibn al-Shihnah mentioned in the margins of al-Jawahir that al-Hawi al-Qudsi is by Judge Jamal al-Din Ahmad bin Muhammad bin Nuh al-Qabisi al-Ghaznawi, the Hanafi, who died around 600 AH. It is called al-Qudsi because he composed it in Jerusalem. I transmitted it from the handwriting of his student Hasan bin Ali al-Nahwi. End. Thus al-Kashf narrator transmitted it, then he said: I saw on the back of a copy of it: that its author, Imam Muhammad al-Ghaznawi, its beginning is 'Praise be to Allah who guided us to the religion of Islam...' etc. End. Then al-Kashf narrator mentioned al-Hawi al-Zahidi, it is Mukhtar bin Mahmud al-Ghazmini, its beginning is 'Praise be to Allah who clarified the landmarks of the sciences...' etc. Then he mentioned: al-Hawi fi al-Furu' by Najm al-Din Abu Shuja' and Abu al-Fada'il Bakir al-Turki, died 652 AH. Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note from the author of Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, listing several 'Hawī' works—comprehensive legal compendia—in the Hanafi tradition. It begins by noting a work by Ibn Ibrahim al-Hasiri (d. 500 AH), a student of Shams al-A'imma, with biographical details. The author then remarks on a third Hawī, 'Hawī al-Zāhidī', whose author is the same as the compiler of the well-known work al-Qunyah, noting its rarity. He then quotes Ibn al-Shihnah's marginalia on al-Jawahir about 'Hawī al-Qudsī', composed by Qadi Jamal al-Din al-Ghaznawi (d. ca. 600 AH), so named because written in Jerusalem. The author also transmits from al-Kashf a note on a copy of that work, and then mentions another 'Hawī al-Zāhidī' by Mukhtar al-Ghazmini, and 'Hawī al-Furū'' by Najm al-Din Abu Shuja' and Bakir al-Turki (d. 652 AH). Finally, he cites Ibn Amir Hajj's statement that the author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi was a Farghani. This entry serves to document the existence and authorship of key Hanafi compendia, helping scholars identify and locate works cited in later fatwa collections.

Key Terms
الحاوي (al-Hawi): A comprehensive legal work that collects rulings from multiple sources; a type of fiqh compendium.
الحاوي القدسي (al-Hawi al-Qudsi): A specific Hawi compendium composed in Jerusalem by Qadi Jamal al-Din al-Ghaznawi (d. ca. 600 AH).
حاوي الزاهدى (Hawi al-Zahidi): A title used for at least two distinct Hawi works: one by the author of al-Qunyah, and another by Mukhtar al-Ghazmini.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which 'Hawi' work is attributed to the author of al-Qunyah according to the passage?
A) al-Hawi al-Qudsi
B) Hawi al-Zahidi
C) Hawi al-Furu'
D) Hawi al-Ghazmini

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi tradition includes multiple distinct 'Hawi' compendia; a mufti must identify the exact work and author to correctly assess the authority of a cited ruling.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Al-Zahiriyya: A Hanafi Work with a Defective Chain
Biographical entry on a Hanafi source

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author of al-Zahiriyya and explain why its attribution is contested within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Zahiriyya is attributed to Ali al-Marghinani but its chain is defective; treat it with caution.

In Hanafi scholarship, the reliability of a source is tied to its transmission chain. This lesson examines al-Zahiriyya, a fiqh work whose authorship is disputed despite its attribution to the elder Marghinani. Understanding this defect is crucial for a mufti evaluating its rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and author
Note that al-Zahiriyya is attributed to Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Marghinani (Zahir al-Din al-Kabir), the father of the famous al-Hasan, author of al-Hidaya. This identity is stated explicitly in the text.
Al-Qari is cited as the source of this attribution.
2
Recognize the transmission defect
The author immediately qualifies the attribution as 'defective' (مخدوش). This means the chain of transmission from the author to later scholars is problematic or unknown.
The defect is significant enough that the reader is referred to al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya for details.
3
Apply the caution in iftaa
As a mufti, you must treat rulings from al-Zahiriyya with caution. They cannot be relied upon unless corroborated by stronger sources (Zahir al-Riwayah or later authoritative texts).
This illustrates the principle of source hierarchy: defective works are not mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح
وستمائة، وانتهت إليه رياسة العلم بعد الست مائة
•
وذكر القارى أن الظهيرية لظهير الدين الكبير على بن عبد العزيز المرغيناني والد الحسن بن على لكنه مخدوش كما ذكر في الفوائد في ترجمة على بن عبد العزيز . راجع الفوائد الظهيرية" في الكتب .
The books mentioned in the commentary. 293. And he reached the presidency of knowledge after six hundred. And al-Qari mentioned that al-Zahiriyya is by al-Zahir al-Din al-Kabir Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Marghinani, the father of al-Hasan ibn Ali, but it is defective as mentioned in al-Fawa'id in the biography of Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz. Refer to al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya among the books.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is from a biographical section listing key books referenced in the commentary. It notes the book al-Zahiriyya, attributed to Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Marghinani (the elder), father of the famous Hasan al-Marghinani. However, the author indicates that the attribution is disputed (مخدوش), pointing the reader to al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya for details. The entry establishes that this work is a source in Hanafi fiqh but requires caution regarding its transmission.

Key Terms
الظهيرية (al-Zahiriyya): A Hanafi fiqh work attributed to Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Marghinani, but with a defective chain as per the author.
ظهير الدين الكبير (Zahir al-Din al-Kabir): The honorific title of Ali ibn Abd al-Aziz al-Marghinani, the elder scholar and author of al-Zahiriyya.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Al-Iqd al-Farid and Its Author: Al-Shurunbulali's Defense of Taqlid
Introduces al-Iqd al-Farid and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and subject of al-Iqd al-Farid and explain its significance in Hanafi ifta usul.

Core Idea
Taqlid is defendable in Islamic law, and this treatise champions it.

This passage introduces al-Iqd al-Farid, a concise treatise by the eminent Hanafi jurist al-Shurunbulali. It defends the permissibility of taqlid (following a madhhab) against those who demand direct ijtihad for every case. Understanding this work is essential for a mufti operating within the Hanafi tradition, as it provides the scholarly basis for relying on established rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work
Locate the full Arabic title: al-‘Iqd al-Farid fi Jawaz al-Taqlid. Note that it is a treatise (risala) on the permissibility of taqlid.
2
Identify the author
The author is al-Hasan ibn Ammar al-Shurunbulali. Note his other works: Imdad al-Fattah (commentary on Nur al-Idah), the matn of Nur al-Idah, and a commentary on Ibn Wahban's versification.
Al-Shurunbulali is a key figure in later Hanafi scholarship.
3
Note the death date
He died in 1069 AH. This places him in the 11th century AH, a period of mature Hanafi fatwa literature.
Refer to the collector 'al-Shurunbulaliyya' for his works.
4
Understand the significance
Taqlid is a foundational usul concept. Al-Iqd al-Farid defends it, making it a vital reference for muftis who follow the Hanafi school. Recognize that the work is not about creed but about fiqh methodology.
This distinguishes it from unrelated works on 'aqida.

Al-Babarti and the Distinctive Contribution of Al-Inaya
Biography of al-Babarti and description of al-Inaya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the unique feature of al-Inaya (supplying the major premise) and explain its importance for a mufti's use of al-Hidaya.

Core Idea
Al-Inaya completes the proofs of al-Hidaya by supplying the missing major premise (kubra).

This lesson introduces you to one of the most important commentators on al-Hidaya, Akmal al-Din al-Babarti. His commentary, Al-Inaya, is prized for a single, crucial feature: it fills in the major premise (kubra al-dalil) that al-Marghinani often omitted from his proofs. Understanding this role deepens your appreciation of how Hanafi scholars construct legal arguments and why a mufti must consult multiple layers of commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its author
Clearly state that al-Inaya is a commentary on al-Hidaya by al-Babarti. Note the full name: Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad al-Babarti.
2
Locate the distinctive feature
Find the sentence that says al-Babarti 'mentions the major premise (kubra) of the proof which the author of al-Hidaya often does not mention.' This is the key merit.
The Arabic phrase: 'يذكر كبرى الدليل الذي لا يذكره صاحب الهداية'
3
Understand the significance for usul and iftaa
Reflect on why supplying the kubra matters: it completes the syllogism, making the legal reasoning fully explicit. A mufti relying on al-Hidaya alone might miss the general principle and misapply the ruling.
In Hanafi usul, a proof (dalil) often comprises a minor premise (saghra) and major premise (kubra). Al-Hidaya sometimes states only the saghra.
4
Survey the biography
Note al-Babarti's teachers (Abu Hayyan, al-Isfahani), students (al-Sayyid al-Sharif, al-Fanari), and his refusal of judgeship. Understand that he was a towering scholar of many arts.
His death year 786 AH places him in the 8th century, a period of rich Hanafi scholarship.
5
Resolve the minor genealogical dispute
Recognize that there is disagreement about whether his father's name is Mahmud or Muhammad, and whether his grandfather is Ahmad or Mahmud. Note that this does not affect the authority of his works.
The passage mentions al-Kafawi and al-Suyuti's accounts; the variation is a common biographical nuance.

Al-Inaya: It is a commentary on 'al-Hidaya' in two volumes by al-Akmal al-Babarti, and it is an easy and useful commentary in the margins of 'Fath al-Qadir'. One of the author's practices in it is that he mentions the major premise (kubra) of the proof, which the author of al-Hidaya often does not mention. Al-Shami said in Radd al-Muhtar: He is the verifier, the shaykh, Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad al-Babarti. He was born in the early 700s (AH). He studied under Abu Hayyan and al-Isfahani, and heard hadith from al-Dalasi and Ibn al-Hadi. He was a scholar of many arts, abundant intellect, strong character, great dignity. Under him studied the eminent al-Sayyid al-Sharif and al-Fanari; judgeship was offered to him but he refused. He authored tafsir, commentary on al-Mashariq, commentary on Mukhtasar Ibn al-Hajib, commentary on Aqida al-Tusi, al-Inaya commentary on al-Hidaya, commentary on al-Sirajiyya, commentary on Alfiyya Ibn Ma'ati, commentary on al-Manar, commentary on Talkhis al-Ma'ani, and al-Taqrir commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi. He died in 786 AH; the sultan and others attended his janaza, and he was buried in al-Shaykhuniyya in Egypt. End. I say: There is disagreement about the name of his father and grandfather. Al-Qari and al-Suyuti in al-Bughya like al-Shami: Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad ... etc., making his father Mahmud and his grandfather Ahmad. Al-Kafawi mentioned his father as Muhammad and his grandfather as Mahmud, and this is mentioned in Husn al-Muhadara by al-Suyuti, so understand. Then al-Babarti (with fathta on both ba's, between them an alif, and sukun on the important ra, then a above-pointed ta): a relative attribution to 'Babarta' (shortened), a village in the vicinity of Baghdad. Thus it was recorded by Imam Wali Allah al-Dihlawi in al-Intibah and al-Suyuti in Lub al-Lubab. Al-Shami said in Radd al-Muhtar: He is the imam, the verifier, the shaykh Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad al-Babarti, born in the early 700s, studied under Abu Hayyan and al-Isfahani, heard hadith from al-Dalasi and Ibn Abd al-Hadi. He was a scholar of many arts, abundant intellect, strong character, great dignity. He has a special merit in his commentary: the author of al-Hidaya often mentions the minor premise without the major, so the author of al-Inaya brings the major premise that the author of al-Hidaya did not mention. This commentary is distinguished by this among other commentaries. Under him studied al-Sayyid al-Sharif and al-Fanari; judgeship was offered but he refused. He authored tafsir, commentary on al-Mashariq, commentary on Mukhtasar Ibn al-Hajib, commentary on Aqida al-Tusi, al-Inaya commentary on al-Hidaya, commentary on al-Sirajiyya, commentary on Alfiyya Ibn Ma'ati, commentary on al-Manar, commentary on Talkhis al-Ma'ani, and al-Taqrir commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi. He died in 786 AH; the sultan and others attended his janaza, and he was buried in al-Shaykhuniyya in Egypt. End. I say: There is disagreement about the name of his father and grandfather. Al-Qari and al-Suyuti in al-Bughya like al-Shami: Muhammad ibn Mahmud ibn Ahmad etc., making his father Mahmud and his grandfather Ahmad. Al-Kafawi mentioned his father as Muhammad and his grandfather as Mahmud, and this is mentioned in Husn al-Muhadara by al-Suyuti, so understand. Then al-Babarti (with fathta on both ba's, between them an alif, and sukun on the important ra, then a above-pointed ta): relative to Babarta (shortened), a village near Baghdad. Thus it was recorded by Shaykh Wali Allah al-Dihlawi in al-Intibah and al-Suyuti in Lub al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This biographical entry provides a detailed account of Akmal al-Din al-Babarti (d. 786 AH), his teachers, students, and works, with special emphasis on his commentary al-Inaya on al-Hidaya. The passage highlights the unique feature of al-Inaya: al-Babarti supplies the major premise (kubra) of the proofs that al-Marghinani (author of al-Hidaya) often omitted, making the commentary particularly valuable for understanding legal reasoning. The discussion also notes a disagreement over the names of al-Babarti's father and grandfather—whether Mahmud or Muhammad—reflecting a minor but significant genealogical debate. This entry is typical of the author's method: it not only lists the book but also provides scholarly biography and critical notes, aiding the student in understanding the authority of the sources.

Key Terms
العناية شرح الهداية (al-‘Inaya Sharh al-Hidaya): Al-Babarti's commentary on al-Hidaya, distinguished for supplying the major premise (kubra) of proofs omitted by the original author.
كبرى الدليل (kubra al-dalil): The major premise of a legal proof, which al-Babarti supplies to complete the arguments of al-Hidaya.
البابرتي (al-Babarti): The nisbah of Akmal al-Din Muhammad, referring to the village Babarta near Baghdad.

Al-Ayni and His Commentary Ramz al-Haqaiq
Biographical entry with critical evaluation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of al-Ayni's biography and evaluate the critique of sectarian bias in his commentary.

Core Idea
Even a great Hanafi scholar's work can be flawed by bias; source criticism is essential.

This passage introduces Badr al-Din al-Ayni, a towering Hanafi scholar, and his commentary Ramz al-Haqaiq. While praising his vast learning, the author notes a significant drawback: 'the smell of sectarian fanaticism.' Understanding this helps us approach his work with caution.

Guided Path
1

Locate the title of the commentary and the full name of the author. This establishes what is being introduced.
The commentary is an expansion on Kanz al-Daqaiq.
2
Note the author's credentials
List the scholarly attributes mentioned: imam, hadith master, historian, linguist, etc. This establishes authority.
Al-Ayni was quick in writing and had broad insight.
3
Recognize the critique
Identify the phrase 'ولو لم يكن فيه رائحة التعصب المذهبي' and understand its meaning: a criticism of sectarian fanaticism.
This is a key point for source evaluation.
4
Understand the implication
Reflect on how this critique affects the reliability of the commentary, especially when dealing with inter-madhhab issues.
Al-Ayni's work remains valuable but must be used with awareness.

Ibn al-Humam and Fath al-Qadir: A Key Hanafi Authority
Biographical listing of a key Hanafi commentator and his work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Ibn al-Humam as a mujtahid of the later Hanafi school and state the significance of his work Fath al-Qadir for fatwa.

Core Idea
Ibn al-Humam's Fath al-Qadir is a premier commentary on al-Hidayah, authored by a recognized mujtahid.

This lesson introduces a foundational text for Hanafi fatwa: Fath al-Qadir by Ibn al-Humam. Knowing its author's high scholarly standing—he was considered a mujtahid by contemporaries—helps you properly weigh his opinions in the school's later hierarchy. The passage also clarifies a linguistic detail about the title.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name
Note the author's full name: Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Abd al-Hamid ibn Mas'ud, famously known as Ibn al-Humam. Recognize his nisbas: al-Hanafi, al-Iskandari, al-Siwasi.
2
Record his birth and death dates
He was born in Alexandria in 788 AH (or 790 AH) and died on Friday, 7 Ramadan 861 AH in Cairo.
The slight uncertainty in birth year is noted in the source.
3
Understand his scholarly status
The passage cites al-Shami and others affirming that Ibn al-Humam was among the 'ahl al-tarjih' (people of preference) and even considered a mujtahid by some contemporaries. This elevates his commentary above mere transmission.
Ijtihad here means ability to derive rulings directly from primary sources, a high rank in later Hanafism.
4
Recognize his major works
His most famous work is Fath al-Qadir, a commentary on al-Hidayah. He also authored al-Tahrir in usul al-fiqh and others.
5
Interpret the title's linguistic nuance
The 'lam' in 'al-Humam' stands in for the possessive; the complete epithet is 'Hammam al-Din,' which was actually the title of his father, Abd al-Wahid. Thus 'Ibn al-Humam' means 'son of (the one titled) Hammam al-Din'.
This clarifies a common confusion about the name.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٩٦ - فتح القدير : للإمام كمال الدين محمد بن عبد الواحد بن عبد الحميد ابن مسعود، الشهير بـ ابن الهمام"، الحنفى، الإسكندري السيواسي، ولد في الإسكندرية سنة ٧٨٨هـ وقيل : ۷۹۰هـ ، ومات يوم الجمعة سابع رمضان سنة ٨٦١هـ بالقاهرة. وصنف التصانيف الكثيرة المقبولة كلها معتبرة ، منها : الشرح المسمى بـ فتح القدير للعاجز الفقير" ، و "التحرير" في الأصول، وغير ذلك . وقال الشامي في الردّ : هو من أهل الترجيح كما أفاده في قضاء البحر، بل صرح بعض معاصريه بأنه من أهل الاجتهاد، ولا سيما قد أقره على ذلك في البحر" و "النهر " و المنح و رمز المقدسي و الشارح ، وهم أعيان المتأخرين فافهم. قلت : وقد قال مولانا عبد الحى : هو رأى نجيح تشهد بذلك تصانيفه وتأليفه . فائدة : ذكر الحموي في "الأشباه " : أن اللام الداخلة على الهمام عوض عن المضاف إليه وهو جزء علم أى همام الدين " ذكر الطحطاوي في شرح الدر المختار " وابن أبي شريف المقدسي في "شرح المسايرة " : أن همام الدين لقب لوالده عبد الواحد .
96 - Fath al-Qadir: By Imam Kamal al-Din Muhammad ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Abd al-Hamid ibn Mas'ud, famously known as Ibn al-Humam, the Hanafi, the Alexandrian, the Sivasi. He was born in Alexandria in 788 AH (or 790 AH) and died on Friday, the 7th of Ramadan, 861 AH in Cairo. He authored many acceptable works, all of them reliable, including the commentary called 'Fath al-Qadir li al-'Ajiz al-Faqir' and 'al-Tahrir' in Usul, and others. Al-Shami said in al-Radd: He is among the people of tarjih as indicated in Qada' al-Bahr. Rather, some of his contemporaries declared that he is among the people of ijtihad, especially since he was affirmed in that by al-Bahr, al-Nahr, al-Munah, and the symbol of al-Maqdisi and al-Sharih, and they are prominent later scholars, so understand. I said: And Mawlana Abd al-Hayy said: It is a sound opinion, as evidenced by his works and writings. Benefit: Al-Hamawi mentioned in al-Ashbah: that the lam entering upon 'al-Humam' compensates for the possessive construct, and it is a part of the title, i.e., Hammam al-Din. Al-Tahtawi mentioned in Sharh al-Durr al-Mukhtar and Ibn Abi Sharif al-Maqdisi in Sharh al-Musayarah: that 'Hammam al-Din' is the epithet of his father Abd al-Wahid.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic entry listing a major Hanafi work, Fath al-Qadir. The text identifies the author as Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Humam, a leading Hanafi jurist of the later period. It gives his birth and death dates, and notes that he was considered by contemporaries to be a mujtahid, meaning he could derive rulings directly from primary sources. The entry then clarifies a linguistic point about the title: the 'lam' in 'al-Humam' replaces the possessive, so the full name is 'Hammam al-Din', which was actually the epithet of his father. This work is a commentary on al-Hidayah and is considered a key reference for Hanafi fatwa, as indicated by the endorsements from later scholars like al-Shami.

Key Terms
ابن الهمام (Ibn al-Humam): The author of Fath al-Qadir, a prominent Hanafi jurist from the 9th century AH.
فتح القدير (Fath al-Qadir): A celebrated commentary on al-Hidayah by Ibn al-Humam, widely used for fatwa.

Listing a standard Hanafi inheritance manual

Core Idea
Al-Fara'id al-Sirajiyya is the standard Hanafi inheritance manual, widely commented upon.

Knowing the classic texts of the Hanafi school is essential for any student of fiqh. This lesson introduces you to one of the most important works on inheritance law (fara'id), which has been the subject of countless commentaries and is still used as a textbook today.

This indicates its authoritative status in Hanafi inheritance studies.
4
Place it in the curriculum
This manual is a standard textbook for learning the science of fara'id in the Hanafi school. It covers the rules of inheritance shares, including Quranic heirs, residuaries, and calculations.

Introducing al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya: 500 Hanafi Maxims
Bibliographical introduction to a collection of Hanafi qawaid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author, structure, and significance of al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya in the Hanafi fatwa tradition.

Core Idea
A mufti's toolbox: 500 Hanafi maxims distilled from the sea of fiqh.

This lesson introduces you to one of the most important collections of Hanafi legal maxims (qawaid). Al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya was compiled by the great Hanafi jurist Zayn ibn Nujaym, renowned for his commentary al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. This work cements the principles that guide fatwa across the madhhab, providing concise rules for consistent ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
Read the title and the description. Note that the book is named after its author, Zayn ibn Nujaym, who also wrote al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
The full title is al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya al-Multaqata min al-Fara'id al-Husayniyya.
2
Understand the scope: 500 maxims
The text explicitly says 'khams mi'at dabitah' (five hundred maxims). These are concise legal rules (dawabit) that govern many specific cases.
This number indicates the work is comprehensive but concise.
3
Context of composition
Zayn ibn Nujaym wrote these maxims while working on his commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically when he reached the section on void sales (al-bay' al-fasid). This shows the practical need for general rules.
The timing hints that maxims are especially useful when dealing with complex transactions.
4
Lack of indexing and its reason
The author did not index the maxims into chapters because 'the rules are mostly not fixed' — meaning many maxims apply across multiple topics, making rigid categorization impractical.
This reflects the flexible nature of legal maxims.
5
Significance for fatwa
This collection is a key reference for muftis. It distills core Hanafi principles that can be applied to new cases, ensuring consistency and adherence to the madhhab.
Mastering these maxims is essential for sound fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
-۹۸ الفوائد الزينية : هي "الفوائد الزينية الملتقطة من الفرائد الحسينية " في مذهب الحنفية، كتاب مختصر على خمس مائة ضابطة، ألفه صاحب البحر حين وصوله في شرح الكنز إلى تبييض البيع الفاسد سميت به نسبة إلى مؤلفها زين بن نجيم صاحب البحر، والزينية نسبة إلى زين الدين على ما هو الأصل في النسبة إلى صدر المركب الإضافي، ولم يبوبه المصنف لعدم انضباط القواعد غالبًا ، أوله : "أحمد الله على الفقه في الدين " ، كذا في الكشف . والله أعلم .
98 - al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya: They are 'al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya al-Multaqata min al-Fara'id al-Husayniyya' in the Hanafi madhhab, a concise book of five hundred maxims, authored by the author of al-Bahr when he reached in his commentary on al-Kanz to the section on void sales. It is named after its author Zayn ibn Nujaym, the author of al-Bahr. The attribution 'al-Zayniyya' is to Zayn al-Din as is the rule in attributing to the first part of a compound name. The author did not index it because the rules are mostly not fixed. Its beginning: 'Ahmad Allah ala al-fiqh fi al-din'. So is it in al-Kashf. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage describes a compilation of 500 Hanafi legal maxims (dawabit) called al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya. The author is Zayn ibn Nujaym, famous for his work al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. He compiled these maxims while writing his commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically when reaching the topic of void sales. The work is a collection of concisely phrased rules that guide fatwa. The title is derived from the author's name Zayn al-Din. The passage notes that the author did not organize them into chapters because maxims often do not fit into fixed categories.

Key Terms
الفوائد الزينية (al-Fawa'id al-Zayniyya): A collection of 500 Hanafi legal maxims by Zayn ibn Nujaym.
ضابطة (ج. ضوابط) (dabitah (pl. dawabit)): A concise legal rule or maxim that governs a set of related cases.
قاعدة (ج. قواعد) (qa'idah (pl. qawaid)): A general legal principle from which multiple rulings can be derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Distinguishing al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya
Bibliographic entry distinguishing two Hanafi works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and identify its author, compiler, and completion date.

Core Idea
Al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya is a separate work from al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya despite the similar name.

In Hanafi literature, works with similar names can cause confusion. This passage introduces al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya, a collection of benefits compiled by Muhammad al-Bukhari, and explicitly states it is not the same as his better-known al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya. Understanding this distinction is essential for accurate referencing and attribution in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
Read the entry and note the full title and author: al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyya by Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Umar Zahir al-Din al-Bukhari (d. 619 AH).
The author is the same as that of al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya.
2
Note the compilation source and completion date
The work is compiled from al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Husami and completed in Dhul Hijjah 618 AH.
This gives a timeframe for the work.
3
Distinguish from a similarly named work
The passage explicitly says 'hiya ghayr al-fatawa al-zahiriyya' – it is different from the fatawa collection. The fatawa collection was mentioned earlier in the original source.
This is the key claim to remember.
4
Recognize the alternative attribution
Some attribute the work to Zahir al-Din al-Hasan al-Marghinani, the teacher of Qadi Khan. This indicates scholarly uncertainty.
Be aware of both attributions when researching.

Al-Qunyah: A Refined Hanafi Manual and Its Author's Theological Controversy
Listing a Hanafi manual compiled from Munyat al-Fuqaha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the relationship between al-Qunyah and Munyat al-Fuqaha, identify the author's background, and evaluate the impact of the author's theological controversy on the work's authority in fatwa practice.

Core Idea
Al-Qunyah refines Munyat al-Fuqaha, but author's suspected Mu'tazilism may affect its acceptability for some scholars.

This lesson introduces al-Qunyah, a Hanafi fiqh manual compiled by Najm al-Din al-Zahidi. It is a refinement (tahdhib) of his teacher's work, Munyat al-Fuqaha. While the author was a great jurist, a theological controversy surrounds him: some scholars considered him a Mu'tazilite. Understanding this context helps a mufti assess the weight of his manual in fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work
Note the full title 'Qunyat al-Munyah li Tatmim al-Ghunyah' and the meaning of 'al-Qunyah' as gain or sufficiency.
The title indicates the work aims to complete the seeker's sufficiency.
2
Identify the author
Note his name: Mukhtar ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad, Abu al-Raja, Najm al-Din al-Zahidi al-Qazmini, died 651 AH. He was a prominent Hanafi jurist.
He was a student of Badi' ibn Mansur al-Iraqi.
3
Understand the relationship to Munyat al-Fuqaha
Al-Qunyah is a tahdhib (refinement/abridgment) of Munyat al-Fuqaha by his teacher. It is not an independent work but a summary.
Tahdhib implies improvement and selection, not a critical edition as we know it.
4
Note the theological controversy
Allamah Ibn Wahban accused al-Zahidi of being a Mu'tazilite. This raises questions about his theological orthodoxy, though his fiqh was respected.
The controversy does not necessarily invalidate his fiqh works but may affect their acceptance by some Hanafi scholars.
5
Assess the practical implication for a mufti
When relying on al-Qunyah, a mufti should verify the ruling with other authoritative Hanafi sources (Zahir al-Riwayah) to ensure it aligns with Sunni doctrine and the madhhab.
The mufti's duty is to give fatwa based on the strongest evidence; personal theological views of the author are secondary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱01 - القنية : (بضم القاف وكسرها كما في المنجد). وهي " قنية المنية لتتميم الغنية لمختار بن محمود بن محمد، أبي الرجاء، نجم الدين الزاهدى القزميني، المتوفى سنة ٦٥١هـ . توجد ،مطبوعة، وهي تهذيب لكتاب " منية الفقهاء " لأستاذه العلامة بديع بن منصور العراقي من فقهاء القرآن السابع . وكان من كبار الأئمة وأعيان الفقهاء، عالماً كاملا ، له اليد الباسطة في الخلاف والمذهب، والباع الطويل فى الكلام والمناظرة. لكن عند العلامة ابن وهبان هو معتزلی
101 - al-Qunyah: (with damm on the qaf and kasr, as in al-Munjid). It is 'Qunyat al-Munyah li Tatmim al-Ghunyah' by Mukhtar ibn Mahmud ibn Muhammad, Abu al-Raja, Najm al-Din al-Zahidi al-Qazmini, who died in 651 AH. It is printed. It is a refinement of the book 'Munyat al-Fuqaha' by his teacher, the Allamah Badi' ibn Mansur al-Iraqi, among the jurists of the seventh century. He was one of the great imams and prominent jurists, a complete scholar, with extensive skill in legal disagreement and the madhhab, and great competence in dialectics and debate. However, according to Allamah Ibn Wahban, he was a Mu'tazilite.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This entry presents al-Qunyah, a Hanafi fiqh manual by Najm al-Din al-Zahidi. The title means 'the gain of the desire to complete the sufficiency'. It is an abridgment and refinement of his teacher's work, Munyat al-Fuqaha. The passage praises the author's expertise in khilaf (juristic differences) and debate, but notes a controversial point: Ibn Wahban considered him a Mu'tazilite in theology. This is important for evaluating the weight of his fatwas, as a theological deviation may affect acceptance of his rulings according to some.

Key Terms
القنية (al-Qunyah): A Hanafi fiqh work by Najm al-Din al-Zahidi, refining Munyat al-Fuqaha.
التهذيب (al-tahdhib): Refinement or abridgment; al-Qunyah is a tahdhib of Munyat al-Fuqaha.
المعتزلة (al-Mu'tazilah): A theological school that emphasizes reason and free will; its adherents are called Mu'tazilites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relationship between al-Qunyah and Munyat al-Fuqaha?
A) al-Qunyah is an independent work.
B) al-Qunyah is a commentary on Munyat al-Fuqaha.
C) al-Qunyah is a refinement of Munyat al-Fuqaha.
D) They are the same book.

Key Takeaway
Al-Qunyah is a refined Hanafi manual, but its author's suspected Mu'tazilism requires the mufti to use caution and verify rulings with more authoritative sources.

Introduction to the 500 Maxims of Ibn Nujaym
Describing the main book of 500 maxims and its author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the matn of 500 maxims, its author, and explain its significance for Hanafi fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
The 500 maxims of Ibn Nujaym form the foundational qawa'id text for Hanafi fatwa methodology.

This passage introduces the core text of the commentary you are studying: a collection of 500 legal maxims (qawa'id) by Ibn Nujaym, known as Sahib al-Bahr. Understanding the origin and structure of this matn is essential for navigating the commentary and for mastering Hanafi fatwa methodology. The author chose not to chapter the book, reflecting the organic nature of qawa'id.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and its content
The passage describes a concise book on 500 maxims. Identify the exact description: 'مختصر على خمس مائة ضابطة'.
This book is the matn being commented upon.
2
Identify the author and his famous work
The author is 'صاحب البحر' (Sahib al-Bahr), i.e., Ibn Nujaym, who wrote the famous fiqh commentary 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq'.
Ibn Nujaym is a central figure in later Hanafi scholarship.
3
Understand the naming and nisba
The book is sometimes called 'al-Zayniyya' after the author's name Zayn al-Din. Learn the rule of nisba to the first part of an idafa compound.
Zayn al-Din is his laqab.
4
Note the absence of chapters
The author did not chapter the book due to the difficulty of organizing the rules systematically. This reflects the nature of qawa'id as interconnected principles.
Memorization and mastery require holistic understanding.
5
Locate the opening phrase
The book begins with 'أحمد الله على الفقه في الدين'. This is a typical basmala and hamdala.
Knowing the opening helps in citing the text.

Commentary
This passage introduces the main book that is the subject of the commentary, which is a collection of 500 legal maxims (qawa'id) written by Ibn Nujaym (known as Sahib al-Bahr, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq). The book is sometimes called al-Zayniyya after its author Zayn al-Din. The commentator notes that the author did not organize it into chapters because the maxims are often not easily categorized. The opening line of the book is given. This information is taken from al-Kashf, a bibliographic work. For a student of Usul al-Ifta, knowing this text is crucial as it forms the basis of the commentary being studied.

Key Terms

مختصر على خمس مائة ضابطة (Mukhtasar 'ala Khams Mi'at Dabitah): A concise work containing 500 maxims; this refers to the matn 'Rasm al-Mufti' or 'al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir' by Ibn Nujaym.
صاحب البحر (Sahib al-Bahr): Title of Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a major Hanafi fiqh commentary.
الزينية (al-Zayniyya): A nisba for the book, derived from the author's name Zayn al-Din.

The Hierarchy of Hanafi Reference Works in Iftaa
List of Hanafi reference works with author and authority notes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi reference works mentioned in the commentary and explain their authority status (mufta bihi, reliable but rare, etc.).

Core Idea
A book's reliability for fatwa depends on its transmission and availability, not merely its content.

This passage from the commentary lists several books invoked in explaining al-Quduri's text. Understanding which books are primary and which are secondary (or rare) is crucial for a mufti to weigh rulings. The author also corrects misconceptions, such as regarding al-Muhit al-Burhani.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure
The passage lists books with numbers (115-119). Each entry gives the title, author, and key characteristics.
2
Extract key details for each entry
For each book, extract: title, author, death date, and its status (e.g., famous, rare, used for fatwa or not).
Focus on authority level: Zahir al-Riwayah, mufta bihi, or scarce.
3
Distinguish mufta bihi from rare works
Note which books are operative for fatwa (e.g., Tanwir al-Absar, Ghurar) and which are reliable but not used due to scarcity (e.g., al-Muhit al-Burhani).
The passage emphasizes that scarcity does not imply unreliability.
4
Identify corrections of misconceptions
The author corrects Ibn Nujaym's mistaken attribution of Majmu' al-Nawazil and clarifies that al-Muhit is not unconsidered but rare.
This highlights the importance of verifying attributions and transmission chains.

The books included in the commentary include his book: Tanwir al-Absar, a magnificent matn in fiqh, abundant in benefit, meticulously thorough in its issues, blessed with fortune, so it became famous in the regions. Its commentary is called Manh al-Ghaffar, one of the most beneficial books of the madhhab. Several people undertook its commentary, among them: al-Haskafi, mufti of Damascus; Mulla Husayn ibn Iskandar al-Rumi, resident of Damascus; and Shaykh Abd al-Razzaq. He died in late Rajab of the year 1004 AH (1596 CE) at age 65. 115 - Matn al-Ghurr by Mulla Khusraw: It is Ghurar al-Ahkam by Mulla Khusraw, Muhammad ibn Faramuz ibn Ali, a famous matn with a commentary by the author called al-Durar. See: al-Durar wa al-Ghurr. 116 - al-Mujarrad: By al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, the Imam, companion of Imam Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). He studied with Abu Yusuf and Zufar, and he wrote the book al-Mujarrad. Born in 166 AH, died in 204 AH. See: al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a (2/52) and Tarikh Baghdad (7/314). The author of Kashf did not mention al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan al-Lu'lu'i. However, he mentioned al-Mujarrad among the Hanafi furu', by Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn al-Hasan ibn Abd Allah al-Bayhaqi, who abridged al-Mabsut, al-Jami'an, and al-Ziyadat, then commented on it and called it al-Shamil; and by Imam Zufar ibn Hudhayl, and he attributed it to the book al-Khuntha from Bada'i' al-Sana'i' by al-Kasani. 117 - Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn: A book that collected the versified issues of al-Quduri with additions, arranged in excellent order, brilliantly concise. At the end of each book it mentions the issues that stray from it related to that topic. It is among the works of Shaykh Ibn al-Sa'ati al-Baalbaki Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Tha'lab al-Baghdadi al-Hanafi, died 694 AH. For more, see 'the author of al-Majma' in al-A'lam. 118 - Majmu' al-Nawazil: A fine book on Hanafi furu', by Shaykh Imam Ahmad ibn Musa ibn Isa ibn Mamun al-Kashi. He was a jurist, debater; he adhered to Najm al-Din Umar al-Nasafi, learned from him, and his stature rose. Ibn Nujaym thought it was by Ali al-Kashi, but it is not, as Taqi al-Din pointed out. Its beginning: 'Praise be to Allah who honored us with the master of the chosen...'. It mentions that he compiled it from fatwas, including: Fatawa Abi al-Layth al-Samarqandi, Fatawa Abi Bakr ibn Fadl, Fatawa Abi Hafs al-Kabir, and others. These chapters were arranged based on fifteen 'principles'. Al-Kashi (with dropping of the nun, mentioned by the author of Kashf in two places: attribution to 'Kash', a village three farsakhs from Jurjan on the mountain. Al-Kafawi mentioned it with an extra nun after the shin, attributing to 'Kashan' (with fatha on kaf and shin). 119 - al-Muhit: It is apparent from its unqualified mention that it is al-Muhit al-Burhani in Hanafi fiqh, because the author of al-Hilya said: 'If al-Muhit is mentioned unqualified, it refers to al-Muhit al-Burhani.' Also, this narration mentioned by the author is found in al-Muhit al-Burhani; I saw it therein, and it is present in the library of Mazaahir al-Ulum in eight large volumes. It is by Allama Burhan al-Din Mahmud ibn al-Sadr al-Sa'id Taj al-Din Ahmad ibn al-Sadr al-Kabir Burhan al-Din Abd al-Aziz ibn Umar ibn Maza al-Bukhari al-Marghinani (born 551 AH, died 616 AH). He was among the great imams and foremost jurists of the Ummah, a pious, striving, humble, perfect imam, an overflowing ocean, an excellent scholar. Ibn Kamal Pasha counted him among the mujtahids in issues. Know that the Hanafis besides the mentioned al-Muhit al-Burhani have three or four al-Muhits by Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi as has passed. Shaykh al-Anwar said in Fayd al-Bari that there are two al-Muhits: first, al-Burhan by the grandfather of the commentator of al-Wiqaya; Mawlana Abd al-Hayy mentioned it is in forty volumes, but I saw it in five volumes; second, by Shaykh Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi. End. Al-Muhit al-Burhani is a reliable book accepted by scholars, as verified by Mawlana Abd al-Hayy in al-Fawa'id. It is not among the unconsidered books as some thought. This is supported by what is in al-Kashf when mentioning al-Dhakhira: 'Both are accepted by the scholars.' End. It is only that issuing fatwa from it is not permitted because it is rare and scarce in that era, not because it is a collection of wet and dry as claimed, for its issues are refined and its branches are structured.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic listing of major Hanafi reference works cited in the commentary. It begins by describing Tanwir al-Absar by the author himself (likely Ibn Nujaym), with its commentary Manh al-Ghaffar, noting the scholars who wrote glosses. The first entry (115) introduces Matn al-Ghurr by Mulla Khusraw, a famous text with a commentary called al-Durar by the same author. Entry 116 discusses al-Mujarrad by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, a direct student of Abu Hanifa who also studied with Abu Yusuf and Zufar. The note clarifies that the author of Kashf did not mention this work, but another al-Mujarrad exists by al-Bayhaqi and Zufar. Entry 117 describes Majma' al-Bahrayn wa Multaqa al-Nahrayn by Ibn al-Sa'ati, a concise collection of Quduri's masail with additions, arranged by chapter and noting exceptions. Entry 118 covers Majmu' al-Nawazil by Ahmad al-Kashi, a compilation of fatwas from various early Hanafi teachers. The passage corrects Ibn Nujaym's mistaken attribution to Ali al-Kashi. Entry 119 discusses al-Muhit, clarifying that the unqualified term refers to al-Muhit al-Burhani by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani. It stresses the book's reliability and acceptance among scholars, explaining that the reluctance to use it for fatwa is due to its rarity, not any defect in its contents. The passage provides author birth/death dates and references for further study.

Key Terms
المحيط البرهاني (al-Muhit al-Burhani): A comprehensive Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (d. 616 AH), considered reliable but rarely used for fatwa due to scarcity.
تنوير الأبصار (Tanwir al-Absar): A matn on Hanafi fiqh by Ibn Nujaym, widely used as a mufta bihi text.
الغرر (al-Ghurr): Ghurar al-Ahkam by Mulla Khusraw, a matn for Hanafi fiqh with a self-commentary al-Durar.
مجمع البحرين (Majma' al-Bahrayn): A concise collection of Quduri's versified masail with additions, by Ibn al-Sa'ati.
مجموع النوازل (Majmu' al-Nawazil): A collection of fatwas by Ahmad al-Kashi, compiled from various early Hanafi sources.
المجرد (al-Mujarrad): A work by al-Hasan ibn Ziyad al-Lu'lu'i, a companion of Abu Hanifa; another by al-Bayhaqi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is fatwa not given from al-Muhit al-Burhani?
A) Its contents are unreliable and mixed with weak opinions.
B) It is too large and complex for easy reference.
C) It was lost and scarce in the later period, not due to any defect.
D) The author was not a trusted scholar.

Key Takeaway
A book's authority for fatwa is determined by its transmission and acceptance, not its size or complexity; scarcity may limit its use but does not negate its reliability.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Bibliography Heading in a Hanafi Fatwa Commentary
Section heading introducing a bibliography

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose of the bibliography heading in a Hanafi fatwa commentary and explain why source hierarchy matters for mufti methodology.

Core Idea
A mufti's authority rests on knowing which books are zahir al-riwayah.

This brief heading, 'al-Kutub al-Waridah fi al-Sharh', appears in Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti to introduce a list of authoritative Hanafi works. While it may seem minor, it signals the commentator's commitment to grounding his fatwa methodology in the core texts (zahir al-riwayah). For students of iftaa, understanding what follows is essential: the hierarchy of sources determines which rulings are operative (mufta bihi) and which are merely historical.

Guided Path
1
Read the heading in context
Note that this is a section heading, not a ruling. It tells the reader that the author will now list the primary Hanafi works he relies on.
Such headings help structure the commentary and orient the student.
2
Understand the function of a bibliography in a fiqh text
A bibliography here is not decorative; it establishes the epistemological weight (zahir al-riwayah vs nawadir) of the sources used in the commentary.
The mufti must cite from the most reliable transmissions.
3
Connect to fatwa methodology (Rasm al-Mufti)
The work being commented on (Uqood Rasm al-Mufti) outlines the rules for issuing fatwas. One key rule is that the mufti must base his answers on the authoritative texts (mutun mu'tamadah). This heading reminds us that the list is part of that framework.
Knowing the hierarchy prevents error in fatwa selection.
4
Reflect on the implied principle
The heading implies that not all Hanafi works carry equal weight. The commentary will highlight which ones are relied upon, and this is a core lesson for anyone learning iftaa.
This is a memorization anchor: remember that source hierarchy is fundamental.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب الواردة في الشرح
The books mentioned in the commentary
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This is a section heading from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti, where the author lists the principal Hanafi works that he relies upon or references in his commentary. It functions as a bibliography, orienting the reader to the authoritative sources that underpin his fatwa methodology.

Key Terms
الكتب الواردة في الشرح (al-Kutub al-Waridah fi al-Sharh): A section heading meaning 'the books mentioned in the commentary', introducing a list of authoritative Hanafi texts.

Key Takeaway

Al-Muntaqa: Combining Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir in Hanafi Source Hierarchy
Biographical and bibliographical entry for al-Muntaqa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the significance of al-Muntaqa in Hanafi fiqh and apply its classification (Zahir al-Riwayah vs Nawadir) to the fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Al-Muntaqa uniquely combines Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, making it a key secondary source in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

This lesson introduces the book al-Muntaqa by al-Hakim al-Shahid, a foundational reference in the Hanafi school. Understanding its content—which includes both the core transmitted rulings (Zahir al-Riwayah) and rare transmissions (Nawadir)—is essential for navigating the levels of authority in Hanafi fatwa. The author's biography and the book's compilation method highlight the rigor of early Hanafi scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book and author
Locate the title 'al-Muntaqa' and its author, al-Hakim al-Shahid. Note his full name and the story of his martyrdom.
This establishes the work's provenance.
2
Distinguish the two categories of content
The text states that al-Muntaqa contains 'masa'il Zahir al-Riwayah' and 'masa'il al-Nawadir'. Understand the difference: Zahir al-Riwayah are the core transmitted rulings of the school, while Nawadir are rare or less authoritative transmissions.
This distinction is crucial for assessing legal authority.
3
Trace the compilation source
Al-Hakim examined 300 volumes, such as al-Amali and Nawadir of Ibn Sam'ah, to select the contents. This demonstrates the selective and scholarly nature of the work.
Note the breadth of sources used.
4
Recognise the book's authority in later works
Later scholars like al-Hamawi and al-Sarakhsi cite al-Muntaqa. Al-Sarakhsi mentions it in al-Muhit after citing Nawadir, indicating its place in the hierarchy.
This shows the work's continued relevance.
5
Note the existence of another work with the same title
The entry mentions a second 'al-Muntaqa' by Ali al-Farghani, author of al-Hidayah. Be careful not to confuse the two.
This avoids bibliographic error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنتقى : لصاحب الكافي ، الحاكم، العالم الكبير، محمد بن محمد ابن أحمد بن عبد الله المروزي ،البلخي، الشهير بـ الحاكم الشهيد " ، قتل ساجداً في ربيع الآخر سنة ٣٣٤هـ . وكان يتمنى الشهادة ويدعو لها. وفى الأشباه : قال الحاكم : "نظرت في ثلاث مائة جزء مثل الأمالي " ، و "نوادر" ابن سماعة حتى انتقيت كتاب "المنتقى " . قال الحموى فى شرحه : "هذا الكتاب من أجل كتب المذهب. فيه مسائل ظاهر الرواية، ومسائل النوادر . ولهذا يذكره رضى الدين السرخسي في المحيط بعد نقل النوادر . وقال المولى المتبحر علی ،چلپی قاضی العسكرين : ولا يوجد المنتقى في هذه الأعصار " . وللحاكم كتب أخرى منها المختصر، والإشارات. وهو في الحديث تلميذ الإمام أحمد رحمه الله بواسطة أبي رجاء محمد بن حمدويه . وقد مر ذكره في "الكافي" في فهرس الكتب . ملحوظة : هناك " المنتقى آخر، لعلى بن أبي بكر الفرغانی، صاحب " الهداية" ، أحد أئمة الفقهاء . وله "التجنيس " و "المزيد " . توفى سنة ٣٤٤هـ . قد مر ذكره مفصلا في الهداية في الكتب .
Al-Muntaqa: by the author of al-Kafi, al-Hakim, the great scholar, Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Abd Allah al-Marwazi al-Balkhi, famously known as al-Hakim al-Shahid. He was killed while prostrating in Rabi' al-Akhir in the year 334 AH. He used to desire martyrdom and pray for it. In al-Ashbah: al-Hakim said: 'I examined three hundred volumes like al-Amali and Nawadir of Ibn Sam'ah until I selected the book al-Muntaqa.' Al-Hamawi said in his commentary: 'This book is among the greatest books of the madhhab. It contains issues of Zahir al-Riwayah and issues of Nawadir. For this reason, Radi al-Din al-Sarakhsi mentions it in al-Muhit after citing Nawadir.' The erudite master Ali Chalpi, Qadi al-Askarayn, said: 'Al-Muntaqa is not found in these times.' Al-Hakim has other works including al-Mukhtasar and al-Isharat. In hadith, he is a student of Imam Ahmad (may Allah have mercy on him) through Abu Raja Muhammad ibn Hamdawayh. His mention has already passed in al-Kafi in the index of books. Note: There is another al-Muntaqa by Ali ibn Abi Bakr al-Farghani, author of al-Hidayah, one of the Imams of the jurists. He has al-Tajnis and al-Mazid. He died in 344 AH. His detailed mention has passed in al-Hidayah among the books.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This is a bibliographical entry from a Hanafi work cataloging important reference books. It introduces the book 'al-Muntaqa' by al-Hakim al-Shahid, a renowned Hanafi jurist who was martyred while prostrating in prayer. The entry highlights that al-Muntaqa is a distinguished compilation because it includes both 'Zahir al-Riwayah' (the core transmitted rulings of the school) and 'Nawadir' (rare and less authoritative transmissions). The author, al-Hakim, derived the book from an extensive study of 300 volumes of previous works, such as the 'Amali' and 'Nawadir' of Ibn Sam'ah. The value of the book is attested by later scholars like al-Hamawi and al-Sarakhsi, and it was so rare that by the time of Ali Chalpi it was no longer accessible. The entry also notes a second 'al-Muntaqa' by a different author, Ali al-Farghani, to avoid confusion.

Key Terms
المنتقى (al-Muntaqa): A selected collection of Hanafi legal rulings compiled by al-Hakim al-Shahid, containing both Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir.
الحاكم الشهيد (al-Hakim al-Shahid): Title of the author Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Marwazi, known as 'the martyred judge' because he was killed while prostrating.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The core transmitted rulings from Abu Hanifa and his major disciples, recorded in six books by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare or less authoritative transmissions that fall outside the core six books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is special about the content of al-Hakim al-Shahid's 'al-Muntaqa'?
A) It only contains Nawadir rulings.
B) It contains both Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir rulings.
C) It is a commentary on the Quran.
D) It is a hadith collection.

Key Takeaway
Al-Muntaqa is a vital secondary Hanafi source that combines core and rare rulings, and understanding its place in the hierarchy is key for proper fatwa derivation.

Identifying the Commentary al-Manh
Bibliographic entry for al-Manh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the full name and author of the commentary al-Manh and state its relationship to al-Tanwir.

Core Idea
Al-Manh is the shortened title; the full name is Manh al-Ghaffar.

This brief entry introduces an important commentary on a foundational Hanafi text. Knowing the correct full title and author ensures precise citation in fatwa work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main subject
Read the first words: 'المنح : شرح التنوير'. Recognize that المنح is a commentary (شرح) on التنوير.
Al-Tanwir is a well-known Hanafi fiqh text by al-Tamartashi.
2
Recognize the full title
Note the phrase 'وتمام اسمه منح الغفار'. The full name of the commentary is Manh al-Ghaffar. 'Al-Manh' is a shortened form.
The entry explicitly gives the complete name.
3
Identify the author
The author is Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Ahmad al-Khatib al-Ghazzi al-Tamartashi. The entry refers to him as 'مصنفه' (its author).
For further details, refer to the entry on 'التنوير'.
4
Determine the work's scope
The commentary is in 'مجلدين ضخمين' (two large volumes), indicating its comprehensive nature.
This suggests detailed exposition of al-Tanwir.
5
Apply in fatwa research
When citing this commentary, use the full title 'Manh al-Ghaffar' and attribute it to al-Tamartashi. This ensures scholarly accuracy.
Proper citation is a duty of the mufti.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنح : شرح التنوير في مجلدين ضخمين لمصنفه وهو محمد بن عبد الله ابن أحمد الخطيب بن محمد بن إبراهيم الخطيب الغزى التمرتاشي وتمام اسمه منح الغفار. ولمزيد الاطلاع على أحوال المصنف راجع متن " التنوير " في فهرس الكتب .
Al-Manh: a commentary on al-Tanwir in two huge volumes by its author, Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Ahmad al-Khatib ibn Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Khatib al-Ghazzi al-Tamartashi, and its full name is Manh al-Ghaffar. For more information on the author's circumstances, refer to the text of al-Tanwir in the index of books.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This entry briefly describes the commentary 'al-Manh' (full title 'Manh al-Ghaffar') on the well-known Hanafi legal text 'al-Tanwir' by al-Tamartashi. The author is Muhammad al-Tamartashi, a Hanafi jurist. The commentary is in two large volumes. The entry directs the reader to the earlier entry on 'al-Tanwir' for biographical details of the author.

Key Terms
المنح (al-Manh): A commentary (sharh) on al-Tanwir by al-Tamartashi, also known as Manh al-Ghaffar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Manh al-Ghaffar
B) Manh al-Ghaffar
C) Sharh al-Tanwir
D) Al-Tanwir

Key Takeaway
The commentary 'al-Manh' is properly titled 'Manh al-Ghaffar', and its author is Muhammad al-Tamartashi.
