Introducing al-Manzuma: Al-Nasafi's Poem on Hanafi Khilafiyyat
Bibliographic entry for al-Nasafi's didactic poem on legal disagreements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify al-Manzuma as a didactic poem on Hanafi legal disagreements and explain its role in mufti training.

Core Idea
Al-Manzuma: a 2,660-line poem memorized to master Hanafi ikhtilafat.

This bibliographic entry introduces a key pedagogical tool in the Hanafi tradition: a poetic work compiling points of legal disagreement within the school. For a mufti, knowing these disagreements is critical for issuing sound fatwas. This lesson will help you place al-Manzuma in the landscape of Hanafi literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his full name and dates.
Extract the author's name, title, birth and death years from the passage.
The author is also known for 'al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah'.
2
Note the work's title and subject matter.
The passage calls it 'al-Manzuma' and states it is a poem on 'khilafiyyat' (matters of disagreement).
This distinguishes it from his creedal work.
3
Count its verses.
The text gives the precise number: 2,660 verses.
4
Identify the commentaries mentioned.
Two commentaries are named: al-Mustasfa and its abridgment al-Musaffa, both by Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi.
Al-Mustasfa is described as a detailed commentary.
5
Understand the work's purpose in Hanafi education.
Such poems were used to memorize points of ikhtilaf, essential for a mufti to know the range of rulings within the school.
This is part of the adab al-mufti training.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المنظومة : هي منظومة الخلافيات" لمفتي الثقلين، العلامة أبي حفص، نجم الدين عمر بن محمد بن أحمد النسفي ، صاحب العقائد النسفية" ، المولود في ٤٦١هـ، والمتوفى سنة سبع وثلاثين وخمس مائة. أولها : باسم الإله رب كل عبد والحمد لله ولى الحمد وعدد أبياتها ألفان وستمائة وستون. ولها شروح كثيرة، منها: شرح صاحب الكنز ، حافظ الدين النسفي المستصفى شرح مبسوط لخصها باسم المصفى . راجع : "المستصفى " في فهرس الكتب .
Al-Manzuma: it is a poem on matters of disagreement (khilafiyyat) by the Mufti of both worlds, the scholar Abu Hafs, Najm al-Din Umar ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad al-Nasafi, author of 'al-Aqa'id al-Nasafiyyah', born in 461 AH, died in the year 537 AH. Its beginning: 'Bismi al-ilahi rabbi kulli abd / wal-hamdu lillahi waliyyi al-hamd'. Its number of verses is two thousand six hundred and sixty. It has numerous commentaries, including the commentary of the author of al-Kanz, Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi, al-Mustasfa, a detailed commentary which he summarized under the name al-Musaffa. Refer to 'al-Mustasfa' in the index of books.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This entry introduces 'al-Manzuma', a didactic poem on legal disagreements (khilafiyyat) within the Hanafi school, composed by the famous scholar Najm al-Din al-Nasafi (also known for his creedal work). The poem contains 2,660 lines. It has several commentaries, notably one by Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi titled 'al-Mustasfa', which was later abridged as 'al-Musaffa'. The entry directs the reader to the index for more on 'al-Mustasfa'.

Key Terms
المنظومة (al-Manzuma): A poetic work by al-Nasafi covering points of legal disagreement within the Hanafi school.
المستصفى (al-Mustasfa): A detailed commentary on al-Manzuma by Hafiz al-Din al-Nasafi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 666
C) 2,660
D) 461

Key Takeaway
Al-Manzuma is a 2,660-line didactic poem by al-Nasafi on Hanafi legal disagreements, used in mufti training and accompanied by major commentaries.

Manzumat al-Hamawi: Understanding Mustadrak in Hanafi Tarjih
Bibliographic note on a didactic poem about Zufar's preferred opinions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify what makes an opinion mustadrak and explain why accurate attribution matters in Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
Not every opinion attributed to a Hanafi master is exclusively theirs; mustadrak corrects misattribution.

This bibliographic entry describes a Hanafi didactic poem listing issues where Imam Zufar's view is preferred. However, the author cautions that some issues are 'mustadrak'—meaning they should be excluded because Zufar's opinion was not exclusive to him. In this lesson, we parse the entry to understand the concept of mustadrak and its role in ensuring accurate tarjih (preference) in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the poem and its purpose
The poem by al-Hamawi lists cases where Zufar's view is preferred in tarjih. Note that tarjih is a process of weighing opinions.
Tarjih is not arbitrary; it follows established criteria.
2
Locate the correction (mustadrak)
The entry says some issues are mustadrak because Zufar did not exclusively hold those views. Identify the Arabic phrase 'لم يختص بها'.
Mustadrak here means 'to be excluded' from the list.
3
Understand the significance
Why does exclusivity matter? In Hanafi tarjih, if multiple scholars hold the same view, it is not a distinctive preference for Zufar. The mustadrak ensures accurate attribution.
Exclusivity confirms that the tarjih is truly for Zufar's unique contribution.
4
Connect to broader Hanafi practice
How does this relate to mufti adab? A mufti must know the sources of opinions and when an opinion is truly representative of a particular scholar.
This prevents misattribution and maintains scholarly integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منظومة السيد الحموي : هي منظومة المسائل التي رجح فيها أصحاب الترجيح قول زفر رحمه الله ، لكن بعض مسائلها مستدرك ؛ لأن زفر رحمه الله لم يختص بها. وهى للعلامة أحمد ابن محمد الحنفي الخموي، صاحب "غمز عيون البصائر حاشية الأشباه والنظائر " . راجع: "أحمد الحموى" في الأعلام.
Manzumat al-Sayyid al-Hamawi: it is a poem on the issues in which the proponents of tarjih gave preponderance to the statement of Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him). However, some of its issues are to be excluded (mustadrak) because Zufar (may Allah have mercy on him) was not specifically associated with them. It is by the scholar Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Hanafi al-Khamawi, author of 'Ghamz 'Uyun al-Basa'ir: Hashiyat al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir'. Refer to 'Ahmad al-Hamawi' in the biographical section.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This entry describes a poem written by Ahmad al-Hamawi (the commentator of al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir) that lists cases where the preferred fatwa in the Hanafi school follows the opinion of Imam Zufar (a prominent early Hanafi jurist). The poem highlights the authority of Zufar's views in certain matters. However, the entry notes that some of the issues included are 'mustadrak' (to be excluded) because they are not exclusively Zufar's views—other scholars also held them. The author is known for his commentary on al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir.

Key Terms
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl, a leading Hanafi jurist whose opinions are sometimes given preference in later tarjih.
مستدرك (mustadrak): Something that should be excluded or is not strictly correct because it does not belong exclusively to Zufar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are some issues in al-Hamawi's poem considered 'mustadrak'?
A) Because Zufar's opinion is not strong.
B) Because Zufar did not specifically hold that opinion exclusively.
C) Because the poem is incomplete.
D) Because the author is unknown.

Key Takeaway
The concept of mustadrak reminds the mufti to ensure that an attributed opinion is truly exclusive to the scholar before relying on it in tarjih.

Ibn Abidin's Poem on Zufar's Preponderant Views
Bibliographic entry for a poem listing Zufar's preponderant views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose, structure, and significance of Ibn Abidin's poem on Zufar's views in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Ibn Abidin's poem lists twenty rare cases where Zufar's opinion becomes mufta bihi, exemplifying the school's layered authority.

This bibliographic entry introduces a unique poetic work by the eminent late Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin. Instead of a typical legal ruling, we learn about a metatextual tool: a twenty-verse poem that enumerates the specific cases where the view of Imam Zufar (a direct student of Abu Hanifa) is given preponderance for fatwa. Understanding this poem helps you appreciate how the Hanafi school prioritises certain narrations within its own ranks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his authority
The poem is by Ibn Abidin, author of Radd al-Muhtar. Recognise his position as the ultimate reference for late Hanafi fatwa.
Ibn Abidin's works are considered the final word in the Hanafi school for muftis.
2
Understand the poem's purpose
The poem collects the only instances where the opinion of Imam Zufar (a senior Hanafi imam) is taken as the mufta bihi (relied-upon) view. Normally, the school follows Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, or Muhammad, but in these twenty cases, Zufar's view prevails.
Zufar's views are typically not preponderant, making this a confined exception.
3
Trace the textual history
The poem originally had 17 verses. Ibn Abidin removed those that were mustadrak (not exclusively Zufar's) and expanded it to 20, following al-Hamawi's model.
The revision shows the living nature of the Hanafi tradition: later scholars refine earlier works.
4
Locate the poem within Radd al-Muhtar
Ibn Abidin inserted this poem in his supercommentary Radd al-Muhtar, specifically in the chapter of Nafaqah (maintenance) in the second volume.
This placement indicates the topical context of many Zufarian exceptions, often related to family law.
5
Reflect on its significance for fatwa practice
The poem serves as a quick-reference for a mufti: in these twenty scenarios, one should adopt Zufar's view, not the standard madhhab position. It operationalises the hierarchy of Hanafi authorities.
Knowing these twenty cases prevents a mufti from issuing a fatwa based on the weaker (marjuh) view when a stronger (Zufar's) is specified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منظومة الشامى : للعلامة ابن عابدين الشامي رحمه الله . هي منظومة فريدة تحتوى المسائل التي رجح فيها قول زفر رحمه الله تعالى. وهي سبعة عشر أسقط العلامة منها ما هو مستدرك، وأوصلها إلى عشرين على ما نظمه العلامة الحموى وقد ذكرها في حاشيته رد المحتار من باب النفقة في المجلد الثاني، تشتمل على عشرين بيتا . أولها : بحمد إله العالمين مبسملا أتوج ،نظمى والصلاة على العلى وبعد فلا يفتي بما قاله زفر سوی صور عشرين تقسيمها انجلی
Manzumat al-Shami: by the scholar Ibn Abidin al-Shami (may Allah have mercy on him). It is a unique poem containing the issues in which the statement of Zufar (may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him) is given preponderance. It consisted of seventeen (verses); the scholar removed from it what was mustadrak and raised it to twenty, according to what al-Hamawi versified. He mentioned it in his gloss Radd al-Muhtar from the chapter of Nafaqah in the second volume. It contains twenty verses. Its beginning: 'Bihamdi ilahi al-'alameen mubasmilan / utawwaju nazmi wa al-salatu 'ala al-'ali / Wa ba'du fala yufta bima qalahu Zufar / siwa suwari 'ishreen taqseemuha anjala'
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This entry describes a poem by the great Hanafi jurist Ibn Abidin (author of Radd al-Muhtar). The poem collects cases where the ruling preferred for fatwa is the one held by Imam Zufar. Initially the poem had 17 verses, but Ibn Abidin removed some that were mustadrak (not exclusively Zufar's) and expanded it to 20 verses, following the pattern set by al-Hamawi. Ibn Abidin included this poem in his famous gloss Radd al-Muhtar, specifically in the section on Nafaqah (maintenance) in the second volume. The first couplet is given, which states that no fatwa should be given according to Zufar's saying except in twenty specified cases.

Key Terms
ابن عابدين (Ibn Abidin): Muhammad Amin ibn Abidin, the authoritative late Hanafi jurist, author of Radd al-Muhtar.
رد المحتار (Radd al-Muhtar): Ibn Abidin's supercommentary on al-Durr al-Mukhtar, the standard reference for Hanafi fatwa.
زفر (Zufar): Imam Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl (d. 158 AH), a senior student of Abu Hanifa and an independent Hanafi jurist.
مستدرك (mustadrak): Something added or overlapping; here, cases where the ruling was not exclusive to Zufar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which section of Radd al-Muhtar did Ibn Abidin place his poem on Zufar's views?
A) Bab al-Tahara
B) Bab al-Nafaqah
C) Bab al-Buyu'
D) Bab al-Talaq

Key Takeaway
Ibn Abidin's twenty-verse poem, placed in the Nafaqah section of Radd al-Muhtar, is the definitive guide to the rare cases where Imam Zufar's opinion becomes the relied-upon view for fatwa.

Mulla Miskin and His Commentary on al-Kanz
Bibliographic entry for a Hanafi commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi commentator Mulla Miskin and explain the meaning of his title.

Core Idea
Mulla Miskin's commentary on al-Kanz is a key Hanafi source; 'Mulla' means scholar in Turkish.

This brief entry introduces the Hanafi scholar Mulla Miskin (Mu'in al-Din al-Harawi) and his commentary on the foundational text al-Kanz. Understanding such bibliographic notes helps you navigate the rich tradition of Hanafi scholarship and identify reliable commentaries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject
Locate the name of the commentary and its author. The title is 'Mulla Miskin's commentary on al-Kanz'.
2
Note the author's full name and death date
The author is Mu'in al-Din al-Harawi, known as Mulla Miskin, who died in 954 AH. This situates him in the 10th century AH.
3
Understand the epithet 'Mulla'
The passage explains 'Mulla' is a Turkish word for 'scholar', with the nūn assimilated into the lām in common pronunciation.
This linguistic note prevents confusion with Arabic words.

The work is a sharh (commentary) on al-Kanz, a standard Hanafi matn. Commentaries expand on the base text and are essential for detailed fiqh understanding.

Munyat al-Mufti: A Compendium of Relied-Upon Hanafi Fatwas
Bibliographic entry for Munyat al-Mufti

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose and methodology of Munyat al-Mufti and evaluate its role in the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Munyat al-Mufti distills relied-upon fatwas by omitting proofs and variant narrations for mufti efficiency.

This lesson introduces you to Munyat al-Mufti, a seminal Hanafi fatwa collection. Understanding its structure and methodology is crucial for navigating later fatwa works. The passage describes how al-Sijistani compiled the book, selecting only relied-upon opinions from multiple sources while omitting proofs and differences for brevity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his purpose
Who is al-Sijistani? What did he aim to achieve with this work?
Author resided in Sivas, died 638 AH.
2
Recognize the sources used
List the works al-Sijistani drew from: Nawadir al-Waqi'at, al-Fatawa al-Sughra, and fatawa of Siraj al-Din al-Ushi.
He summarized Nawadir without proofs.
3
Understand editorial choices
Why did he omit references, superfluous narrations, and differences? What does 'relying upon' mean?
He only included what is 'mu'tamad' (relied upon).
4
Note the arrangement and marks
How did he organize the material? What does the letter 'seen' signify?
He followed the arrangement of al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah and marked additions with س.
5
Evaluate significance for a mufti
How does such a compilation help a mufti in issuing fatwas?
Provides concise, reliable rulings without needing to consult multiple sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منية المفتى : هي في فروع الحنفية للشيخ الإمام يوسف بن أبي سعيد أحمد السجستانی نزیل سیواس، المتوفى ٦٣٨هـ . غير مطبوع . أوله الحمد لله الغنى الخالق . . . إلخ " لخص فيه نوادر الواقعات عرية عن الدلائل وذكر : أنه رأى الفتاوى الصغرى " لنجم الدين الحاجي، وكتب فيه منها ما هو المعتمد عليه وحذف الإحالات وزوائد الروايات والاختلافات قصراً للمسافة، ضم إليها من فتاوى سراج الدين الأوشي، نوادر من الواقعات مما لا يوجد في أكثر الكتب، وصرف الهمة إلى الإيجاز في الألفاظ من غير إخلال وراعى تجنيس الفتاوى السراجية، وميزها بعلامة السين .
Munyat al-Mufti: it deals with the branches of Hanafi fiqh by the Shaykh Imam Yusuf ibn Abi Sa'id Ahmad al-Sijistani, resident of Sivas, died 638 AH. It is unpublished. Its beginning: 'Al-hamdu lillahi al-ghani al-khaliq...' etc. He summarized in it 'Nawadir al-Waqi'at' (Rare Occurrences) free of proofs. He mentioned that he saw 'al-Fatawa al-Sughra' of Najm al-Din al-Haji, and wrote from it what is relied upon, and omitted references, superfluous narrations, and differences for brevity. He added to them from the fatawa of Siraj al-Din al-Ushi, rare occurrences not found in most books, and devoted effort to conciseness of wording without deficiency. He observed the uniform arrangement of al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah and distinguished them with the sign 'seen'.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This entry describes the book 'Munyat al-Mufti', a Hanafi fatwa collection compiled by Yusuf al-Sijistani (d. 638 AH). The author summarized 'Nawadir al-Waqi'at' (a collection of rare cases) without proofs, and also used 'al-Fatawa al-Sughra' by Najm al-Din al-Haji to extract only the relied-upon opinions, omitting references and variant narrations for brevity. He further incorporated fatawa from Siraj al-Din al-Ushi, adding rare cases not commonly found. The work is noted for its conciseness. He arranged the material similar to 'al-Fatawa al-Sirajiyyah' and marked those additions with the letter 'س' (seen). The book remains unpublished.

Key Terms
منية المفتى (Munyat al-Mufti): A concise Hanafi fatwa collection by al-Sijistani, focusing on relied-upon rulings from Nawadir and later fatwa works.
الفتاوى الصغرى (al-Fatawa al-Sughra): A fatwa collection by Najm al-Din al-Haji, used as a source by al-Sijistani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Sijistani do with the rulings from al-Fatawa al-Sughra?
A) He copied all rulings with their proofs.
B) He selected only the relied-upon opinions and omitted references and variants.
C) He translated them into Persian.
D) He only summarized the table of contents.

Key Takeaway
Munyat al-Mufti is a model of efficient fatwa compilation, distilling relied-upon rulings from multiple sources for the practicing mufti.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Key Hanafi Reference Works: Al-Nahr, Al-Hidayah, Al-Waqi'at, and Haruniyat
List of key Hanafi fiqh works with author biographies and descriptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and describe four essential Hanafi reference works, their authors, their content, and their role in fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
Four essential texts form the backbone of Hanafi ifta: al-Nahr, al-Hidayah, al-Waqi'at, and al-Haruniyat.

This lesson introduces four foundational Hanafi texts that every student of ifta should know. The passage from Rasm al-Mufti lists these works with concise author profiles and unique features. Understanding the purpose and method of each text will help you navigate the Hanafi tradition and locate authoritative rulings efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work and its author
For each entry, note the full name of the author, his scholarly credentials, and his historical context. This establishes the authority of the text.
Authors include Ibn Nujaym (al-Nahr), al-Marghinani (al-Hidayah), al-Sadr al-Shahid (al-Waqi'at), and Imam Muhammad (al-Haruniyat).
2
Understand the content and purpose
Read the description to determine what each text contains: is it a commentary (sharh), a collection of cases (nawazil), or a compendium of issues? This tells you how to use the work.
al-Hidayah is a commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi; al-Nahr is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq; al-Waqi'at is a compilation of nawazil; al-Haruniyat is a collection of issues from the time of Harun al-Rashid.
3
Analyze the author's method
Look for clues about how the author presents rulings. For example, al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah first states the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad with evidence, then presents Abu Hanifa's position with its own evidence.
This comparative method is a hallmark of al-Hidayah and essential for understanding ikhtilaf within the school.
4
Note any unique features or mnemonics
Some works include systems for cross-referencing. Al-Waqi'at uses symbols: 'ayn for al-'Uyun, waw for al-Waqi'at, ba for Abu Bakr's fatawa, sin for Samarkand fatawa. Memorizing these aids quick retrieval.
The passage instructs: 'So memorize' (faḥfaẓ) – indicating the importance of these symbols for the mufti.

-١٤٥ النهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق : هو للعلامة الشيخ عمر بن إبراهيم سراج الدين الشهير بـ عمر ابن نجيم " المصرى، وهو أخ صغير لصاحب البحر زين ابن نجيم وهو فقيه محقق، رشيق العبارة كامل الاطلاع، كان متبحراً في العلوم الشرعية ، غواصا في المسائل الغريبة. توفى سنة خمس بعد الألف (١٠٠٥هـ) ودفن عند شيخه وأخيه الشيخ زين الدين (محبى ملخصاً). وله في النهر مناقشات على شرح أخيه، لكن لم يكمله المانع حدث ووصله إلى كتاب القضاء، فصل الحبس" وهو مخطوط، ولخص أنفع الوسائل للطرسوسي " في کتاب باسم "إجابة السائل " .
١٤٦ الهارونيات: الهارونيات : هی مسائل جمعها محمد رحمه الله في زمن هارون الرشيد، كما في حاشية الطحطاوي على المراقى (ص ۱۰). وفي مفتاح السعادة (۱۲۸/۲) : أن الهارونيات مسائل جمعها لرجل مسمّى بهارون .
١٤٧ الهداية : هي "الهداية في الفروع " لعلى بن أبي بكر بن عبد الجليل، الفرغاني، المرغيناني . كان إمامًا، فقيها ، حافظا، محدثا، محققا، أصوليا ، أديبا، شاعراً، توفى سنة ٥٩٢هـ . وهو شرح له على متن " بداية المبتدئ". وعادته أن يحرر كلام الإمامين من الدليل، ثم يحرر مدعى الإمام الأعظم، وبسط دليله.
واعتنى بشرحه جم غفير من العلماء والفقهاء. ومن شروحه : معراج الدراية إلى شرح الهداية لقوام الدين البخارى، و الغاية للسروجى ولم يكمله، و "غاية البيان "
لأمير كاتب الإتقانى . و نهاية الكفاية للإمام المحبوبي .

١٤٨ - الواقعات للصدر الشهيد : هي الواقعات الحسامية : للصدر الشهيد الصدر الماضى الصدر الكبير أبى الصدور، برهان الدين الكبير، ابن مازه برهان الأئمة، حسام الدين أبي محمد عمر بن عبد العزيز بن عمر بن مازه . وهو من أكابر فقهاء الأحناف في القرن السادس. إمام الفروع والأصول، المبرز في المعقول والمنقول، كان من كبار الأئمة وأعيان الفقهاء. له اليد الطولى في الخلاف والمذهب رزق الشهادة في صفر سنة ست وثلاثين وخمس مائة قتله الكافر الملعون بعد وقعة قطعوان بسمرقند ونقل جسده إلى بخارى. وكانت ولادته سنة ثلاث وثمانين وأربعمائة . وكان رحمه الله ،حنفيّا، ومن قال : إنه شافعي فقد توهم . وقد جمع في كتابه "الواقعات " بين "النوازل " لأبي الليث و الواقعات للناطفى، وأخذ من فتاوى أبي بكر محمد بن الفضل، وفتاوى أهل سمرقند . ورتب الكتب كالمختصر المنسوب إلى الحاكم الشهيد، والأبواب كالنوازل، وأشار بالعين إلى مسائل العيون، والواو إلى الواقعات والباء إلى الشيخ أبي بكر، والسين إلى فتاوى سمر قند، فاحفظ

Books mentioned in the commentary

-145 al-Nahr al-Fa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq: by the scholar Sheikh 'Umar ibn Ibrahim Siraj al-Din, famous as 'Umar ibn Nujaym al-Misri. He is the younger brother of the author of al-Bahr, Zayn ibn Nujaym. He was a meticulous jurist, elegant in expression, comprehensive in knowledge, deeply learned in the religious sciences, and a diver into rare issues. He died in the year 1005 AH and was buried near his teacher and brother Sheikh Zayn al-Din (summarized). In al-Nahr, he has discussions on his brother's commentary, but he did not complete it due to an obstacle; he reached the chapter of qada, section of habs. It is in manuscript. He summarized Anfa' al-Wasa'il of al-Tarsusi in a book called 'Ijabat al-Sa'il'.
146 al-Haruniyat: al-Haruniyat are issues collected by Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) during the time of Harun al-Rashid, as in Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 'ala al-Maraqi (p. 10). In Miftah al-Sa'ada (2/128): that al-Haruniyat are issues collected for a man named Harun.
147 al-Hidayah: It is 'al-Hidayah fi al-Furu'' by 'Ali ibn Abi Bakr ibn 'Abd al-Jalil, al-Farghani, al-Marghinani. He was an imam, jurist, memorizer, hadith scholar, verifier, usuli, literary figure, poet. He died in 592 AH. It is a commentary on his own matn 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi'. His habit was to present the statements of the two Imams (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf/Muhammad) with evidence, then present the claim of the Greatest Imam (Abu Hanifa) and elaborate his evidence.
Many scholars and jurists paid attention to its commentaries. Among its commentaries: Mi'raj al-Diraya ila Sharh al-Hidayah by Qiwam al-Din al-Bukhari, and al-Ghayah by al-Saruji (incomplete), and Ghayat al-Bayan by Amir Katib al-Itqani, and Nihayat al-Kifayah by Imam al-Mahbubi.
Also: al-Kifayah fi Sharh al-Hidayah by Mahmud ibn 'Abd Allah Taj al-Shari'a author of al-Wiqayah,
and also by Jalal al-Din al-Khwarizmi with the same name.
Also Kamal ibn al-Humam commented on it and named it Fath al-Qadir li al-'Ajiz al-Faqir, which is among the most famous and most complete commentaries in benefit. Also Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi, and Ibn al-Shihna named it Nihayat al-Nihayah. Also Badr al-Din al-'Ayni named it al-Binayah, and al-Babarti named it al-'Inayah, and likewise al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani, and besides that it has many commentaries.
The hadiths of al-Hidayah were extracted by Imam al-Zayla'i and named it Nasb al-Rayah, and Imam Ibn Hajar summarized it as al-Dirayah fi Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah.
And if you desire detail, refer to the entry 'Sahib al-Hidayah' in the index of notable figures.
(Stray: طوة)
148 al-Waqi'at li al-Sadr al-Shahid: They are al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya: by al-Sadr al-Shahid al-Sadr al-Madi al-Sadr al-Kabir Abu al-Sudur, Burhan al-Din al-Kabir, ibn Maza Burhan al-A'imma, Husam al-Din Abu Muhammad 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Umar ibn Maza. He was among the greatest Hanafi jurists of the sixth century. An imam of furu' and usul, distinguished in rational and transmitted sciences. He was among the great imams and leading jurists. He had a long hand in ikhtilaf and madhhab. He was granted martyrdom in Safar 536 AH, killed by the accursed unbeliever after the battle of Qatwan in Samarkand, and his body was transferred to Bukhara. He was born in 483 AH. He was Hanafi, and whoever says he was Shafi'i has deluded himself. In his book 'al-Waqi'at', he combined 'al-Nawazil' of Abu al-Layth and al-Waqi'at of al-Natafi, and took from the fatawa of Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl and the fatawa of the people of Samarkand. He arranged the books like the Mukhtasar attributed to al-Hakim al-Shahid, and the chapters like al-Nawazil, and indicated with 'ayn for issues of al-'Uyun, waw for al-Waqi'at, ba for Sheikh Abu Bakr, sin for fatawa of Samarkand. So memorize.
Among his works: 1. al-Jami' al-Fatawa al-Sughra, 2. al-Fatawa al-Kubra, 3. 'Umdat al-Mufti wa al-Mustafti, 5. al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya, 6. Sharh Adab al-Qadi, 7. Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir. Manuscripts of these books exist in various libraries. His grandson, Mida Burhan... Mahmud, was also a skilled jurist.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography of key works referenced in this commentary on Rasm al-Mufti. It lists four major Hanafi texts: (145) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq by Ibn Nujaym, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq; (146) al-Haruniyat, a collection of issues from the time of Harun al-Rashid; (147) al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani, perhaps the most famous Hanafi fiqh text; and (148) al-Waqi'at by al-Sadr al-Shahid, a compilation of nawazil (legal cases). Each entry provides the author's full name, scholarly credentials, and key details about the work. The author notes al-Marghinani's method in al-Hidayah of presenting the positions of Abu Hanifa's two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) with evidence, then the position of Abu Hanifa himself with its evidence—a hallmark of comparative fiqh. The many commentaries on al-Hidayah are enumerated, emphasizing its centrality. For al-Waqi'at, the author highlights the system of abbreviations used: 'ayn for 'Uyun, waw for Waqi'at, ba for Abu Bakr, sin for Samarkand fatawa—a mnemonic device for the reader. This passage serves to orient the student of ifta to the authoritative sources they will rely upon.

Key Terms
النهر الفائق (al-Nahr al-Fa'iq): A commentary by Ibn Nujaym on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, known for its precise discussions and critique of the author's brother's work.
الهدارية (al-Hidayah): A foundational text of Hanafi fiqh by al-Marghinani, a commentary on his own matn Bidayat al-Mubtadi, presenting the views of the two Companions and Abu Hanifa with evidence.
الواقعات الحسامية (al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya): A collection of legal cases (nawazil) compiled by al-Sadr al-Shahid, combining earlier works with symbols for cross-referencing.
الهارونيات (al-Haruniyat): Issues collected by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani during the reign of Harun al-Rashid, named either after him or a man named Harun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which famous Hanafi work is known for presenting the positions of Abu Hanifa's two companions with evidence, then Abu Hanifa's own position with evidence?
A) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq
B) al-Hidayah
C) al-Waqi'at al-Husamiyya
D) al-Haruniyat

Key Takeaway
Mastering these four texts—al-Nahr, al-Hidayah, al-Waqi'at, and al-Haruniyat—gives the mufti a solid foundation for navigating Hanafi primary sources and issuing sound fatwas.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Navigating the Structure of Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti
Table of contents for fatwa methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the major sections of a classical Hanafi fatwa methodology text based on its table of contents.

Core Idea
A mufti must know the hierarchy of transmitted rulings, the qualifications for fatwa, and when to depart from Zahir al-Riwayah.

This lesson introduces the structure of a foundational text on Hanafi fatwa procedure. The table of contents reveals the key debates: which books are authoritative, when a mufti can choose, and the role of the school's later scholars. Understanding this roadmap helps you locate and interpret the detailed rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the book's purpose
Recognize that this table of contents organizes topics in Hanafi usul al-ifta — the methodology for issuing fatwas within the Hanafi school.
The term 'Rasm al-Mufti' refers to the discipline of fatwa procedure.
2
Scan major topic clusters
Notice groupings: conditions for fatwa (books, teacher), sources (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir), differences (ikhtilaf al-riwayah), and qualifications.
Headings beginning with 'مطلب' signal distinct sections.
3
Identify the hierarchy of sources
Look for sections that discuss Zahir al-Riwayah vs. other narrations, and the precedence of the Imam's statements over companions' views.
The phrase 'ظاهر الرواية' appears multiple times.
4
Recognize key procedural terms
Terms like 'تخريجات المشايخ', 'ترجيح', 'تصحيح', and 'اختلاف الرواية' are central to fatwa methodology.
These relate to the process of preferring and correcting positions.

فهرس المحتويات
مطلب : الكتب التى لا يجوز الإفتاء بها، ووجوهه ستة .
مطلب : متى يجوز الإفتاء من هذه الكتب
مطلب : لا بد من المراجعة إلى المأخذ الأصلي، وعدم الاعتماد على المأخذ الثانوى
مطلب : لا يجوز الإفتاء لمن طالع الكتب بنفسه ولم يتفقه لدى أستاذ ماهر ، ووجوب تعزير من خالفه . .
مطلب : يجب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه .
مطلب طبقات المسائل ثلاثة .
مطلب في نسخ المبسوط" وشروحه.
مطلب : في الرد على العلامة ابن كمال باشا في فرقه بين ظاهر الرواية ورواية الأصول.
مطلب في تحقيق لفظ "السير"
مطلب : معنى كتب الأصول والأصل
مطلب في سبب تأليف "الجامع الصغير"
مطلب في الفرق بين "الصغير" و "الكبير"
مطلب في وجه تصنيف السير الكبير "
مطلب في الأخذ بما في السير الكبير عند اختلاف الأقوال إلا إذا اختار المشايخ خلافه
مطلب : كافى الحاكم جمع كلام محمد في كتبه الستة التي هي ظاهر الرواية ، ومبسوط السرخسي شرحه
مطلب فى مبسوطات الحنفية .
مطلب في أن مبسوط السرخسى شرح للكافي لا يختصر لمختصر الحاكم
مطلب فى الفرق بين اختلاف القول واختلاف الرواية .
مطلب في بيان الوجوه الخمسة لاختلاف الرواية .
مطلب : يصح نسبة القولين إلى المجتهد ولو رجع عن أحدهما بالكلية ؛ لعدم رفع الخلاف بالرجوع.
مطلب : ما ذكره الأصوليون من عدم إمكان قولين لمجتهد، مشكل ؛ فإن الواقع خلافه
مطلب : أقوال أصحاب الإمام في الحقيقة أقواله، فمن قلدهم لا يخرج عن تقليده .
مطلب : إذا صح الحديث فهو مذهب أبي حنيفة بشرطين .
مطلب : أقوال أصحاب الإمام والمسائل المبنية على العرف والضرورة وتخريجات المشايخ على قواعد الإمام غير خارجة عن المذهب الحنفى
مطلب : تخريجات المشايخ على قواعد الإمام أقرب إلى مذهبه من أقوال الأصحاب
مطلب في الترتيب بين روايات المذهب والحكم فيما إذا خالف الصاحبان الإمام .
مطلب : يجوز اتباع الدليل وترك قول الإمام وإن وافقه أحد صاحبيه. ليس للمفتي في زماننا التخيير والترجيح بل عليه أن يتبع أهل الترجيح والتصحيح
مطلب في الرد على ما قاله صاحب البحر " إنه يجب علينا الإفتاء بقول الإمام وإن أفتى المشايخ بخلافه
مطلب في معنى أهلية النظر والفتوى
مطلب في معنى قول الأئمة : "لا يحل لأحد أن يفتى بقولنا حتى يعلم من أين قلنا؟ " .
مطلب : المحقق ابن الهمام وتلميذه العلامة قاسم من أهل الاجتهاد لا صاحب "البحر "
Table of Contents
Section: The books upon which it is not permissible to issue fatwa, and its aspects are six.
Section: When is it permissible to issue fatwa from these books
Section: It is necessary to refer to the original source, and not to rely on the secondary source
Section: It is not permissible to issue fatwa for one who has studied the books himself but has not studied under a skilled teacher, and the necessity of disciplining those who violate it.
Section: It is obligatory to issue fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah unless they explicitly state otherwise.
Section: The layers of masail are three.
Section: Regarding the abrogation of al-Mabsut and its commentaries.
Section: Refuting Allamah Ibn Kamal Pasha regarding his distinction between Zahir al-Riwayah and Riwayat al-Usul.
Section: Investigating the term 'al-Siyar'
Section: The meaning of Kutub al-Usul and al-Asl
Section: Regarding the reason for authoring al-Jami' al-Saghir
Section: Regarding the difference between al-Saghir and al-Kabir
Section: Regarding the method of categorizing al-Siyar al-Kabir
Section: Regarding taking what is in al-Siyar al-Kabir when there is disagreement among opinions, unless the shuyukh have chosen otherwise
Section: Kafi al-Hakim collected the statements of Muhammad in his six books which constitute Zahir al-Riwayah, and Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is its commentary.
Section: Regarding the Mabsutat of the Hanafis.
Section: Regarding that Mabsut al-Sarakhsi is a commentary on al-Kafi, not an abridgment of Mukhtasar al-Hakim.
Section: Regarding the difference between ikhtilaf al-qawl and ikhtilaf al-riwayah.
Section: Explaining the five aspects of ikhtilaf al-riwayah.
Section: It is valid to attribute two opinions to a mujtahid even if he retracts one entirely, because disagreement is not removed by retraction.
Section: What the usuliyyun have mentioned about the impossibility of a mujtahid having two opinions is problematic, for the reality is otherwise.
Section: The statements of the Imam's companions are in reality his statements, so whoever follows them does not leave his taqlid.
Section: If a hadith is authentic, it is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, with two conditions.
Section: The statements of the Imam's companions and issues based on custom and necessity, and the derivations of the shuyukh upon the Imam's principles, are not outside the Hanafi madhhab.
Section: The derivations of the shuyukh upon the Imam's principles are closer to his madhhab than the statements of the companions.
Section: Regarding the order among the narrations of the madhhab and the ruling when the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oppose the Imam.
Section: It is permissible to follow the evidence and abandon the Imam's statement, even if one of his two companions agrees with him. The mufti in our time does not have the choice and preference; rather, he must follow the people of tarjih and tas-hih.
Section: Refuting what the author of al-Bahr said: 'We must issue fatwa according to the Imam's statement even if the shuyukh have issued fatwa otherwise.'
Section: Regarding the meaning of eligibility for nazar and fatwa.
Section: Regarding the meaning of the imams' statement: 'It is not permissible for anyone to issue fatwa according to our statement until he knows from where we derived it.'
Section: Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam and his student Allamah Qasim are among the people of ijtihad, not the author of al-Bahr.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents from the book 'Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti', listing the various sections (matlab) that are discussed in the following pages. It covers key topics in Hanafi usul al-ifta, including the conditions for issuing fatwa, the hierarchy of sources (Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir), the relationship between the Imam's statements and those of his companions, the role of custom and necessity, and the qualifications of a mufti. The table provides a roadmap for the reader, indicating the major issues addressed in this classical work on fatwa methodology.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The most authoritative layer of transmitted rulings in the Hanafi school, consisting of the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
اختلاف الرواية (Ikhtilaf al-Riwayah): Differences in transmitted versions of a ruling from the early Hanafi imams, often due to multiple narrations.
تخريج (Takhrij): Legal derivation by later scholars (shuyukh) from the principles of the founding imams.
أهلية النظر والفتوى (Ahl al-Nazar wa al-Fatwa): The qualifications required to engage in legal reasoning and issue fatwas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the table of contents, which section indicates when it is obligatory to issue fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) مطلب في الرد على العلامة ابن كمال باشا
B) مطلب طبقات المسائل ثلاثة
C) مطلب: يجب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه
D) مطلب في الفرق بين الصغير والكبير

Key Takeaway
The table of contents reveals that Hanafi fatwa methodology is a science with strict hierarchies and conditions, not mere opinion.
